Minister of Railways Zhang Gongquan Publishes Reflections on Inspecting the Southwest Railways - Direct Access to Guangzhou Possible in the Second Half of Next Year - Guangxi's Poverty Promotes Its Progress

Minister of Railways Zhang Gongquan recently returned to his department after inspecting the Southwest railways. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency obtained his officially published reflections on the inspection as follows: This time, I traveled from Hangzhou to Guangzhou to inspect the railways, spending a total of 21 days on the round trip. Before starting the journey, I had the following hopes: (1) How should we prepare in the future to achieve the goal of direct through train service from Shanghai to Guangzhou? After the inspection, I feel that if there are no unexpected obstacles to the current plan, it can be achieved in the second half of next year. The Qiantang River Bridge is expected to be completed around April or May next year. The bridge construction project had many concerns in the past, but now it is largely not a problem. After the completion of the Qiantang River Bridge, it is hoped that the Yuping Railway can be connected to the Yuehan Railway in June next year. However, at the same time, the light rail section of the Hangjiang line must be replaced with heavy rail. The connection project between the two lines in Hangzhou must also be carried out in parallel in order to realize the hope of direct access between Guangdong and Shanghai. This inspection is intended to contact all parties so that various matters can be prepared quickly and completely. (2) The Yuehan Railway is currently divided into three sections: Xiang-E, Zhu-Shao, and Guang-Shao. However, if it is still divided into separate sections after the upcoming opening to traffic and cannot be managed jointly, it will not only be uneconomical but also difficult to unify management and external relations. Therefore, I went to various provinces to discuss with the local authorities so that they could understand the matter of consolidation. When I arrived in Xiang-E, I first consulted with the two chairmen of the Hubei and Hunan provincial governments. When I arrived in Guangdong, I consulted with Commander-in-Chief Chen. The results were extremely satisfactory. All parties deeply understand the importance of railways to the country and greatly support the unified management of the Yuehan Railway. Therefore, in the near future, the three sections of the Yuehan Railway can be merged into one. Therefore, I have the following reflections: (1) Railways can promote mutual understanding and consensus, and create close relationships between provinces. If the railway crosses several provinces, it is always hoped that they will have the same concept of the railway and cherish it. In the past, various provinces did not understand the railway very well, and there were cases of acting independently. This was the case in Xiang-E, and also in Guang-Shao. The Ministry believes that the provinces cannot cooperate. In fact, we are running the railway business to assist the unity and close relationship of the provinces. The railway authorities cannot think that the responsibility is completed after the construction of the railway. They should still make the provinces understand that the railway is an organization to help communication and unification. Therefore, after the completion of the railway, the Ministry must explain to various places so that there is no separation between provinces and between provinces and the central government. Not only is the flow of goods and passengers smooth, but also the spirit between provinces and between provinces and the central government is communicated, so that it can fulfill its mission. Otherwise, if they each have their own interests and cannot cooperate, it will greatly hinder the future of the railway business. We should help the local authorities to eliminate this kind of obstacle. This is the responsibility of the Ministry and the directors of various railway bureaus, and it is also the biggest reflection after my observation and return. (2) There are too many staff members in various railways. This is because the directors of the bureaus have often been replaced in the past. New directors must use a batch of new people, but the old ones are not easy to remove, and they accumulate more and more. At the same time, their backgrounds are different, so it is impossible for them to fully understand the unified thinking and spirit of the national railway. The thoughts of railway employees across the country are different, so the management and reform plan of the railway are not easy to promote, and training cannot be completed in one day. Then, how to unify their thoughts and spirits? The only way is to personally visit and contact the personnel of each bureau to make their thoughts and spirits change considerably. This is the second point that I feel is necessary to go out for inspection. (3) After this inspection, I feel more deeply the importance of railway construction in our country. The provinces I passed through are all poor and financially exhausted. Even if water conservancy is handled or rural loans are released, the benefits of rural restoration are extremely slow. The agricultural products produced locally are inherently low in value, and it is impossible to transport them by expensive automobiles. Those with more goods are abandoned on the ground, and those with shortages buy goods at high prices. May I ask, in this situation, how can the living conditions of farmers be improved? The so-called method of improving the living conditions of farmers, in addition to raising the prices of agricultural products, there is no more effective method. If we rely on currency to raise prices, China has not yet reached this level. Therefore, only by expanding sales channels and reducing transportation costs can we implement the most basic and universal methods. In the past, Hengzhou eggs were sold for 17 cents per hundred, but now they are sold for more than 40 cents. The reason for the increase in sales price is that the railway has been opened and sales channels have been expanded. From this, we can see that if we want to increase the prices of agricultural products and improve the living conditions of farmers, the quickest and most convenient method is to use the railway. (4) The large-scale production in the southwestern provinces, in addition to agricultural products, is minerals. The development of minerals is originally a source of wealth, but if there is a lack of railway transportation, the output is too large to generate profits. In the southwestern provinces, it is impossible to develop agricultural products at present, but if minerals are developed without railway transportation, not only will the products not have sales channels, but also the development equipment will not be imported. Therefore, I believe that railway construction is extremely related to the recovery of the southwestern economy. In the southwestern provinces, it is really necessary to quickly build railways. At the same time, I feel that future route surveys cannot be based on population, cities, and terrain as the main basis for route surveys. We must develop a certain industry as the standard for route surveys, and we must also consider the economic, national defense, and industrial plans of the entire country, so as to avoid the future being considered inconsistent with the economic plan, re-transforming it, and wasting resources. Therefore, in the future, which province should develop industry, which province should develop agriculture, and which province should develop mining, we must first determine the entire plan, and then the route survey and construction of the railway will have a basis. Therefore, we should have a full understanding and preparation for this view and plan. (5) There are too many personnel in various railways. If we want to reduce them, the cost will be too high, and it will be difficult to continue. The only way is to build more new roads and allocate and transfer the original personnel, which is enough to remedy the disease of overstaffing, and can also conform to the purpose of selecting people for the job, and the adverse phenomena caused by layoffs will not be discovered. In the future, each railway bureau should determine the number of employees, and no arbitrary increase is allowed beyond the number. When there are vacancies in the original personnel, they must not be replenished. At the same time, new roads should use old railway personnel as much as possible. According to this plan, after several years, the personnel and funding problems of the railway may be completely resolved. In addition, after inspecting the two Guangdong provinces, I feel that Guangdong has recently been striving to develop economic construction, and there are many factories established, such as chemical industrial factories, sugar factories, and other industries, but they are all in their infancy. It will take a long time to see the results. The province's economy was difficult last year, but fortunately, overseas Chinese benefited more from the increase in tin prices in Nanyang, so more remittances were sent to Guangdong, which was enough to make up for it slightly. Otherwise, the local economic situation may be more difficult. From an objective point of view, the local taxes in Guangdong Province are too heavy. The provincial government is now trying to remedy it. The only advantage of Guangxi is diligence and thrift. Everyone who goes to Guangxi says that Guangxi is progressing. I don’t know that the reason for its progress is entirely due to poverty. The provincial government's annual income is 30 million yuan (silver dollars), only one-tenth of that of Guangdong. In addition, there is an annual trade deficit of more than 20 million yuan, and its economic and financial difficulties can be known. Therefore, Guangxi cannot but strive to survive in this difficult and difficult environment. When I went to Nanning, I did not see anyone wearing silk clothes or foreign clothes. Therefore, I believe that poverty can promote the progress of a province. The policies and goals implemented by Guangxi are all in line with the Central New Life Movement and the policies established by the Central Government. If those who serve in the Central Government can recognize that our situation has also reached the point of poverty, then progress will be faster. In short, our central government is now living on debt, and has a spirit of working hard in poverty, then the railway business will definitely have great progress. Extending it, if all departments have such ideas, are content with poverty, and are brave enough to work hard, then the central government will definitely prosper, and the progress of the national politics and economy will be immeasurable.

Establishment Meeting of the Ministry of Industries' Fish Market Today

Minister Wu of the Ministry of Industries Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday to Preside Over the Election of Directors, Supervisors, and Managers

The Ministry of Industries' Fish Market, after negotiations between Minister Wu of the Ministry of Industries and Mr. Duesheng, a fish merchant in this city, decided to jointly operate it by officials and merchants. There were twists and turns due to misunderstandings in the Ice-Fresh Fishery Association. After mediation by gentry and merchants, the association's sympathy was obtained, and the shares were fully paid up. The establishment meeting will be held today. Minister Wu, accompanied by the Director of the Fisheries and Animal Husbandry Department, arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning and will attend to preside over the meeting. According to a reporter from the Central News Agency, the details are as follows:

Principle of Joint Operation by Officials and Merchants Decided

The opening of the fish market has been delayed due to changes in the business model. Recently, Wu Dingchang, Minister of Industry, personally came to Shanghai to negotiate with fish merchant leader Du Yuesheng and others and decided to jointly operate it by officials and merchants. The capital was fixed at 1.2 million yuan, half from officials and half from merchants. The subscribers of merchant shares are the Ice-Fresh Fishery Association and the River-Fresh Fishery Association, each for 50,000 yuan, non-fishery merchant shares for 200,000 yuan, and the remaining 300,000 yuan will be temporarily paid by the Ministry of Industry and gradually transferred. Du Yuesheng and Qian Xinzhi were elected as representatives to negotiate separately.

Ice-Fresh Fishery Agrees to Cooperate

The members of the Ice-Fresh Fishery Association initially expressed their unwillingness to cooperate because they were concerned that their own business would be affected, which led to the resignation of the association's president, Du Yuesheng. After emergency consultation by the association, they earnestly retained him. Gentlemen and merchants, such as Yu Yanfang and Fang Jiaobo, invited the managers of various fish shops to talk a few days ago and explained in detail, and they were sympathetic and agreed to cooperate, and each shop voluntarily subscribed for 20,000 yuan of shares. The remaining 30,000 yuan was supplemented by borrowing the association's property. However, the association requested that the business rules of the market be discussed in detail and that the interests of the fish shops be taken into account, which was also accepted by Yu et al., and it was decided to unanimously advocate when discussing the detailed rules.

Fish Industry Conference Advocates Six Points

The association, for the sake of its own interests, held a meeting yesterday and decided on six points to notify the members, solicit their opinions, so as to practically advocate at the shareholders' meeting, and request that clear provisions be added to the detailed rules. The original text of the six points is as follows: The 100,000 yuan owed by the fish market to the Bank of Communications, which is transferred to the association for approval, although there are fish market shares as collateral, is still the responsibility of each member. The shareholders of the fish shops now have the intention of closing down the joint venture fish shops from time to time. It is feared that it will be difficult to agree to solicit consent on this issue. In addition to the shares that each member has subscribed for, the number is insufficient, and it is jointly agreed to maintain the previous proposal and supplement it by borrowing funds from the public office property. The fish market should set up a branch market in the original 16 shops in the fish market center and designate each fish shop as a market affairs officer. All fish should be handled by the market affairs officer fish shop to exercise its powers. Preserve the original loan distribution and sales business of each fish shop. The fish shop exercises its duties as a market affairs officer, limited to 23 companies, and no more will be added in the future. The method of buying and selling is still the original method of successive buying and selling. No matter how the commission is stipulated, each fish shop must still enjoy the original 8%, but the commission for fresh and salted boats will still be handled according to the current commission deduction.

Minister and Director Come to Shanghai to Preside Over

According to reporters from the Central News Agency, the market has determined that the merchant shares are 300,000 yuan, which has been fully collected by the Bank of China, and the official shares of 600,000 yuan have also been paid, and the 300,000 yuan of merchant shares to be paid have also been allocated. Therefore, Xu Tinghu, Director of the Fisheries and Animal Husbandry Department of the Ministry, was dispatched to Shanghai one day in advance to arrange the meeting, and Wu Dingchang, Minister of Industry, also arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning. Director Xu also had a talk with the merchant shareholders Yu Qiaqing, Yu Yanfang, Lin Kanghou, Fang Jiaobo, Shen Tianxin, Zhang Shenzhi, etc. yesterday afternoon and decided to hold the establishment meeting at 2:00 PM today.

Directors and Supervisors Can Be Elected Immediately

The fish market was previously decided to be handled by the Ministry, and the Ministry had appointed directors and managers. Now that the organization has changed, the former manager Yu Kaizhan has resigned and is rushing to hand over. The shareholders' meeting will elect directors to take over. According to the new organization regulations, there are 11 directors, 6 appointed by the Ministry and 5 elected by the merchants. Although the merchant shares have not been fully collected, the distribution of the number of directors will not be changed. The selection of the manager must also be decided by the board of directors. The number of supervisors remains the same as originally determined, with 3 appointed by the Ministry and 2 elected by the merchants. The above-mentioned directors, supervisors, and managers will be elected at the establishment meeting. As for the organizational outline and business rules, they will be approved by the board of directors and submitted to the Ministry of Industry for promulgation and implementation. Its official opening for business is not far away. (Central News Agency)

Shanghai Muslim Groups Welcomed Ma Hongkui Yesterday

Ma...Loved Religion and Country, Talked About...With the Country's Survival, Religion Survives

Several hundred representatives from mosques in Nanmen, Ximen, Xieqiao, Liu Malu, Taopeng Road, Gordon Road, Xiaoshadu, Hongshoufang, Jiangwan, and Rihui Port attended. Chairman Ma has been leading troops for many years and has contributed to the party and the country. This goes without saying. However, Chairman Ma has also wholeheartedly supported religion, Shanghai, and various religious education, charity, and public welfare undertakings. Today's warm welcome is a sincere expression. We hope Chairman Ma will give us guidance." Ma Hongkui then gave a speech, saying, "Shanghai's co-religionists, I am truly undeserving of such kindness. However, in this time of national crisis, we are all citizens and should fulfill our duties to the country with a heart that loves religion, protecting the country. As they say, 'With the country's survival, religion survives; with the country's demise, religion perishes.' As the ancients said, 'If the skin is gone, what will the hair cling to?' I hope to encourage each other with you all." His words were extremely cautionary. Finally, Tie Jun and Ma Tianying also gave speeches. They then visited the newly built building, had some refreshments, and went to the Qinglian Street Muslim Association. After a meeting, the entire group took a photo and dispersed.

China National Products Bank Held the Annual General Meeting Yesterday

Reported on the Operating Conditions of the Previous Year, Distributed Dividends, and Re-elected Kong Xiangxi, Li Hongsheng, and Others as New Directors and Supervisors

Dagong News Agency reports that the China National Products Bank held its sixth annual shareholders' meeting at the Bank Club on Hong Kong Road yesterday afternoon. Shareholders including official shareholders and commercial shareholders such as Mu Ouchu, Tang Shoumin, Xu Kan, Rong Zongjing, Song Liaowen, Li Hongsheng, Qian Xinzhi, Song Ziliang, Huang Yizhu, and others, representing more than 20,000 shares, attended. Xu Kan was elected as the chairman.

Business Report

After the formal opening ceremony, Chairman Xu delivered an opening speech, followed by General Manager Song Ziliang, who reported on the operating conditions for the 24th year of the Republic (1935). He stated that the economic and financial situation in China during the 24th year of the Republic had not improved from the decline of the previous year. Shanghai, as the center of all industries in the country, was particularly affected. It was not until winter that the government resolutely promulgated emergency decrees and implemented the legal tender policy, which stabilized finance and brought about a flourishing trend in industry and commerce. The bank, with its mission, continued to adhere to its consistent principle of stability and soundness, maintaining normal operations for various businesses. It made every effort within its capabilities to protect industry and commerce and promote national products. However, loans to prefectures and counties focused on mortgages, and expenditures were minimized. Fortunately, the annual settlement resulted in modest achievements, which can be gratifying to the shareholders. The annual operating profits and losses are detailed below: (A) Total operating profits for the year amounted to 1,557,860.012 yuan in national currency, including the bank division: interest, 875,943.55 yuan; remittance income, 81,021.26 yuan; handling fees, 30,952.83 yuan; foreign exchange profits, 200,696.26 yuan; securities profits, 219,626.51 yuan; savings division: interest, 4,483.64 yuan; handling fees, 2,649.40 yuan; miscellaneous profits, 7,943.29 yuan; miscellaneous losses, 7,943.29 yuan; securities profits, 5,733.90 yuan. (B) Total losses amounted to 646,809.32 yuan in national currency, including the bank division: various expenses, 460,650.42 yuan; amortization of bad debts, 177,176.97 yuan; savings division: various expenses, 8,981.93 yuan. After offsetting profits and losses, the net profit was 911,050.08 yuan. After deducting 30% of the savings division's public reserve, amounting to 23,348.49 yuan, and including the previous year's surplus of 24,664.52 yuan, the total surplus was 912,366.83 yuan. The full settlement and profit distribution plan for the 24th year are detailed in separate schedules, which are submitted for your review.

Profit Distribution

The profit and dividend distribution is as follows: Public Reserve: 100,000.00 yuan; Appropriation for Start-up Costs: 89,000.00 yuan; Appropriation for Operating Equipment: 65,000.00 yuan; Bad Debt Reserve: 100,000.00 yuan; Average Stock Dividend Reserve: 120,457.70 yuan; Special Reserve Fund: 60,000.00 yuan; Commercial Stock Dividend: 118,626.90 yuan; Shareholder Dividend: 59,542.30 yuan; Remuneration for Directors, Supervisors, and Staff: 180,000.00 yuan; Retained Surplus: 19,739.93 yuan; Total: 912,363.83 yuan.

Newly Elected Directors and Supervisors

The meeting then amended Article 6 of Chapter 2 of the bank's articles of association, which was unanimously approved. Finally, the directors of the third session of commercial shares and the supervisors of the seventh session of commercial shares were re-elected. As a result, Kong Yongzhi, Qian Xinzhi, Song Ziwen, Song Ziliang, Hu Wenhu, Xu Kan, Li Shizeng, Song Zijing, and Xu Xie Kang were elected as commercial share directors. Wu Qiding, Zhou Zuomin, Zhang Zhuyu, Rong Zongjing, and Mu Jiechu were elected as alternate directors. Song Zi'an, Liu Hongsheng, Bian Baimei, and Zhou Shouliang were elected as commercial share supervisors. Yang Desen, Tang Shoumin, Wang YunSong and Huang Nianyi were elected as alternate supervisors. There were also six official share directors and five supervisors to be re-elected, who will be directly appointed by the Ministry of Finance. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM.

Cai Zengji Discusses the Reform of River Steamers

Implementing Ticket Sales at Docks and Limiting Ticket Numbers; Rectifying Sanitary Facilities and Improving Both Freight and Passenger Transportation

Since Cai Zengji took over as General Manager of the state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, he has been actively rectifying and sparing no effort. The reporter from Xinxin News Agency met with Mr. Cai yesterday, and he spoke in detail about the benefits of the company's reforms to passengers and merchants on the river steamers. The details are recorded as follows:

Past Problems of River Steamers

Mr. Cai stated, "Since the company was ordered to reorganize, it has been implementing the Ministry of Communications' rectification plan step by step. Although there are many tasks and it is difficult to achieve success overnight, we are cooperating and working hard to achieve success day by day. The recent reform of river steamers is also one aspect of the rectification plan. In the past, ticket sales for river steamers were not restricted, and passengers often exceeded the number of berths by one or two times. In addition, scattered soldiers and undesirables were mixed in, smoking, gambling, and creating chaos. There was no order on the ship, let alone hygiene. Therefore, due to long-standing habits, the treatment of third-class passengers on river steamers was almost inhuman. Moreover, each ship had at least sixty or seventy teahouse waiters, and as many as one hundred and thirty or forty. The ship workers were not paid wages and relied entirely on privately selling berths and soliciting tips for their services. After purchasing tickets and boarding the ship, third-class passengers had to buy berths from the teahouse waiters before they had a place to rest. Even the official cabins with fixed berths often claimed that they were reserved to extort tips. As for tips for alcohol, they often amounted to more than 30% of the ticket price for long-distance trips, and were even equal to the ticket price for short trips. Outright extortion was rampant. All of these shortcomings were unique to river steamers. Anyone who has traveled on river steamers knows this in detail. Our company is a state-owned shipping agency, and at this time of vigorously promoting the New Life Movement, we must reform and innovate without hesitation."

Various Reform Measures

The various measures after the reform and the expectations for gradual implementation are briefly described as follows: 1. Implementing ticket sales at the docks. In addition to continuing to entrust reputable firms to act as ticket agents, the company will implement ticket sales at the docks in various ports from April 1st. Anyone who has not purchased a ticket will not be allowed to board the ship. From now on, scattered soldiers and undesirables will not be able to enter, and order on the ship will be easily maintained. The previous bad phenomena can be gradually eliminated. In addition, passengers can purchase tickets and board the ship upon arrival at the dock, so even tourists will not have the difficulty of not knowing where to go. They will not have to go through others and suffer unexpected losses. 2. Limiting the number of tickets to prevent overloading. If passengers exceed the number of berths, some passengers will pay the same price for tickets but will not receive the same treatment. Moreover, exceeding the number of people will be dangerous for navigation. Therefore, the number of tickets has been limited, and all berths will be numbered. The principle is that those who purchase a ticket will have a berth. Passengers will not be crowded, and they will not have to worry about not having a berth after purchasing a ticket. 3. Rectifying hygiene on the ship. After the first two items are implemented, passengers will feel comfortable. The company is also striving to rectify hygiene facilities and has invited members of the New Life Movement General Association to station on the ship for guidance to achieve cleanliness and order. This will definitely benefit the health of passengers. 4. Stipulating the salaries and tips for teahouse waiters and prohibiting greed. The drawbacks of hiring teahouse waiters without paying wages have already been described above. Therefore, the company is handling this in accordance with the labor service principle. All teahouse waiters serving on river steamers will be paid a considerable monthly salary so that their personal lives can be solved first. As for tips for alcohol, it will be up to the passengers, although the standard is stipulated to be 10% of the ticket price. However, there should be no dispute if less is given, and greed is absolutely prohibited.

Hoping for Cooperation from All Sectors

The above points are only a glimpse of the matters carried out after the reform. The company will definitely implement them one by one and maintain them forever to demonstrate the spirit of state-owned shipping and fulfill its duty to serve society. However, after limiting the number of tickets, the company will suffer great losses in competition with those who do not limit the number of tickets. All business personnel on the ships, from the chief of affairs to the teahouse waiters, will be paid salaries by the company, so the increase in expenses is a natural result. Therefore, the company bears a huge burden after the reform. The government is willing to make huge sacrifices for the sake of rectifying the shipping industry and seeking the interests of the majority. However, in order to gradually implement the government's rectification plan and promote state-owned shipping, it is hoped that patriotic people will rise up to assist and share the mission. Although the development of shipping companies in other countries is due to good management, how can they achieve this without the cooperation and support of people from all walks of life in their own countries? The reform of the company's river steamers is truly a firm intention to reform the business. In the future, improving freight transportation and rectifying warehouses and docks will be carried out continuously to live up to the expectations of those who care for the company. However, since the company has not hesitated to make huge sacrifices to carry out reforms, it is hoped that people from all walks of life will, with patriotic enthusiasm, extend their love to the company for the benefit of both freight and passengers, so that the company's business can develop day by day. Then, even if there are some sacrifices at present, it is hoped that the benefits will be reaped in the future. As for all the measures of the company, if passengers have any opinions, or if there are any oversights, it is hoped that they will teach us. Thank you very much.

The Ministry of Finance Responds to the Chamber of Commerce That Documents Internally Compiled Should Be Stamped, Distinguishing Between Scattered and Compiled Orders

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce previously requested the Ministry of Finance to exempt internal documents that do not create rights and obligations from stamp duty after they are used and compiled into a book. Yesterday, it received a reply from the Ministry of Finance, Tax Document No. 9145, stating, "Both telegraphs from Xian and Ma have been noted. Article 11 of the Stamp Duty Rate Table, under the nature column for books and registers used by businesses, stipulates that all general and branch books and registers established by shops or banks in relation to their business belong to this category. Moreover, Article 11 of the Detailed Rules stipulates that books and registers compiled from loose leaves should still be stamped according to the example for books and registers. The so-called books and registers refer to all books and registers related to business. The original article does not call them account books but books and registers, and the intention is here. If the documents used internally are bound into a book, then they are the same style and have the same effect as other books and registers, and they cannot be called books and registers that are not related to business. The previous approval of the Ministry for internal documents that are compiled into a book and stamped according to the example for books and registers is in accordance with the provisions of Article 11 of the Stamp Duty Rate Table and Article 11 of the Implementing Rules, and is not an illegal collection. Moreover, the documents used internally are intended for notification or reporting when used individually, but after being compiled into a book, the purpose of use is to check the accounts, which is the same as the purpose of using books and registers. Since books and registers should be stamped before use, these documents should also be handled in the same way when compiled into a book, which is not in conflict with the provisions of Article 5 of the Stamp Duty Law. In short, there is no problem with internal documents that are compiled using paper wrappers or tied with rope, and are not made into the style of books and registers. Otherwise, they should still be handled according to the example for books and registers in order to prevent abuses. This approval is hereby transferred for your information."

Merchants Unite to Transport Less-than-Carload Freight; Shippers Now Responsible for Escorting Goods; Standardized Escort Measures Established

According to the Central News Agency, the Ministry of Railways notes that practices vary across railway lines regarding whether shippers are responsible for escorting less-than-carload freight. This inconsistency creates difficulties in handling through freight. To facilitate merchants and promote through freight, standardized measures have been established. An order has been issued to inform all railway lines that, in accordance with Article 7 of the General Rules for Goods Transportation (except for flowers and trees), and in accordance with Business Circular Freight Category No. 12, goods transported with a minimum charge equivalent to 2,000 kilograms do not require an escort. The railway will take care of them along the way, but will not be responsible for losses. If the shipper applies and wishes to send an escort, it should be handled in accordance with Article 41 of the General Rules for Goods Transportation. The above measures will be implemented from May 1st of this year. It is reported that the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations have been ordered to instruct their traffic departments to comply.

Young Couple Attempt Suicide Due to Love and Poverty

Tan Shenghua and Wu Aifang Unable to Secure Betrothal Gifts Lead to Tragedy

The Wu Palace Hotel at 152 Fuzhou Road, Fujian Road, received a young couple the day before yesterday. They checked into the hotel together. The hotel clerk guided them to room 631. The man, who identified himself as Tan Shenghua, 23 years old, from this area, a businessman, and the woman, Wu Aifang, 18 years old, retired early that night. However, around 7 AM yesterday, the tea attendant heard cries coming from the room, mixed with vomiting. He knocked on the door, but received no response after a long time. Sensing something was wrong, he reported to the clerk, who managed to climb in through the transom window. He found both of them rolling in bed, their faces pale. The bedding was stained with blood and traces of poison. Two empty poison bottles were on the table next to the bed. Realizing they had attempted suicide by poison, he immediately reported to the police station and had them rushed to the hospital for treatment. Their conditions were critical. Police officers found a note left by the couple in room 631, which read, "Please notify Xu Shenshan of the International Telegraph Office immediately." Based on this note, the police began an investigation. It was learned that the man's name was indeed Tan Shenghua, residing at 1 London Road, Zhabei, and had worked for the Dada Automobile Company, a Japanese firm on Avenue Foch [now East Yan'an Road]. He had been unemployed since the January 28 Incident. The woman had studied at Deqing Girls' Primary School, residing at 4 Xiang'an Lane, Bao'an Road, Zhabei. The couple had known each other for a long time and had developed a close relationship. After their relationship was discovered by their parents, marriage was discussed. However, Tan was unable to afford the betrothal gifts due to financial difficulties. The woman's family repeatedly pressed for the gifts in the shortest possible time. Tan had no choice but to propose postponing the engagement, scheduled for February 23rd of this year. However, busybodies mocked him, claiming that Tan was intentionally delaying, intending to abandon her. The cold irony was jarring to the ear. Wu Aifang's parents were displeased and scolded their daughter. Feeling aggrieved, Wu ran away from home and went to Tan. After discussing the situation, they believed they would never be able to live together. The emotions of love and depression collided, leading to this tragedy. The poor customs drove two young people to resort to this drastic measure. It is truly lamentable.

The Franconia Carries World Cruise Members to Shanghai Yesterday

A 144-Day Journey Through 19 Countries and 35 Ports

The Franconia, a British world cruise ship managed by Thos. Cook & Son, belongs to the Cunard Line. The ship, with a gross tonnage of 20,000 tons, is equipped with unparalleled luxury. It has sailed on world cruises six or seven times. It departed from New York on January 7th, arriving at Le Brea, then proceeding to Brazil in South America, then Jamestown, and rounding the Cape of Good Hope to South Africa. It visited Madagascar and Sicily, then proceeded to Ceylon, the Dutch East Indies, and finally Hong Kong and Shanghai. The places it visited in Africa were rarely visited by previous cruises. This trip aroused the interest of adventure among the cruise members.

Delayed Arrival in Shanghai

The ship was originally scheduled to arrive at Wusong on the night of the 8th, but was delayed due to fog at sea. It finally arrived at Wusong at 12:55 PM yesterday. Thos. Cook & Son sent a pilot to guide the ship into the port. It berthed at the Gonghexiang Wharf at 2:30 PM, twelve hours behind schedule. Three representatives from Thos. Cook & Son also took a launch to Wusong to greet the cruise members and discuss the itinerary.

Sightseeing Itinerary

Three hundred and fifteen cruise members arrived, including the famous explorer Mr. Burke. Mr. Burke was most interested in this trip to South Africa. The ship docked at Gonghexiang Wharf at 2:30 PM yesterday. Thos. Cook & Son had prepared a large number of cars, which transported the cruise members to various parts of the city and Jiangwan for sightseeing. In the evening, they had dinner at the Cathay Hotel. This morning, they boarded the ship to Qinhuangdao, visiting Tianjin and Beijing. Some of the cruise members will fly to Nanjing and then to Beiping for a few days, seeing the Great Wall.

Return to the United States

After visiting the north, the Franconia will proceed to Japan, cross the Pacific Ocean to Honolulu to see the Kilauea Volcano, then to Los Angeles, California, before returning to New York via the Panama Canal. The ship departed on January 7th and will return to the United States on May 29th, covering over 40,000 nautical miles, passing through 19 countries and 35 ports in 144 days.

Gu Gengmei Sues Lin Xianglin for Embezzlement

Aftermath of Property Grab Case

Lin Xianglin, residing at 24 Qiantou, Yongjia County, Wenzhou, schemed to seize his uncle's inheritance. He fraudulently obtained a savings certificate worth $50,000 from his cousin Lin Xinying. Fearing that Lin Xinying's husband, Gu Gengmei, would interfere, he bribed Wang Rusong, an officer of the Yongjia Public Security Bureau, with $350. He also instructed Lin Xinying to falsely accuse Gu Gengmei of embezzlement at the Public Security Bureau. The case was discovered by the director of the bureau, who handed over Wang Rusong, Lin Xianglin, and others to the Yongjia District Court. After interrogation, Wang Rusong was sentenced to two years and six months in prison for accepting bribes. Lin Xianglin was sentenced to one year in prison for instigating false accusations. It has been learned that Gu Gengmei recently hired lawyer Liu Shifang to file a lawsuit with the Shanghai First Special Court's Criminal Division, accusing Lin Xianglin of embezzlement. The main points of the lawsuit allege that the defendant, Lin Xianglin, is the cousin of Gu's wife, Lin Xinying. He had long coveted the assets of the plaintiff's mother-in-law and repeatedly sowed discord in front of Xinying. The plaintiff went to Wenzhou in the autumn of the 22nd year of the Republic [1933] to serve as the director of the Ouhai Hospital and resided there with his wife. At the same time, he often went to Shanghai.

Visiting His Mother

The defendant took the opportunity to slander Xinying, falsely claiming that the plaintiff had an affair in Shanghai. Falling for the scheme, Xinying entrusted the defendant to come to Shanghai in November of last year, bringing back to Wenzhou the contract savings book seals stored at the Shanghai Bank and the Tongyi Trust Company. He also handed over the key to the safety deposit box at the Shanghai Bank and the seal used to open the box. The defendant arrived in Shanghai on the 24th of the same month and went to the Shanghai Bank and Tongyi Trust Company's safety deposit box to remove all the gold placed inside. This included a savings [amount] of $500 in the name of Gu Gengmei at the Continental Bank, two savings books in the name of Gu Gengmei at the Shanghai Bank, each with $500, and 70 taels, 1 mace, and 7 fen of gold, totaling $7,999.38 in national currency. This savings and gold were the plaintiff's private property and unknown to Xinying. Therefore, Xinying did not entrust him to bring them back. The defendant planned to embezzle them. He withdrew the savings and interest from the two banks.

Withdrew the Full Amount

(totaling $1,579.73 in national currency) and sold the gold. He never handed over the two items to Xinying. In February of this year, the plaintiff went to the Shanghai Bank to open the safety deposit box and found that the savings book and gold were gone. He learned that it was the defendant who had done it. His actions constitute the crime of embezzlement under Article 335 of the Criminal Code. He requests judgment ordering the defendant to repay the plaintiff $9,579.11 in national currency, plus interest. Yesterday afternoon, judge Zhan Liangce presided over the hearing of the case in the Ninth Criminal Court. Because the defendant's residence is

In Yongjia County

Therefore, there are still questions regarding jurisdiction. Fishing Disturbance in Yu Garden, Jiangwan

One Person Caught Stealing Fish, Chinese Police Interfere, Over Ten Village Women Injure Police Officer

Last night at approximately 9 PM, the gardener of Yu Garden Fish Pond on Jiangwan Road, Zhabei, discovered villagers intruding to steal fish. He chased after them and apprehended one person on the spot, calling the police to take him to the station. A Chinese police officer from Hongkou Park interfered. At the same time, a village woman gathered a crowd of over ten people who blocked the road and acted violently. One police officer was injured. The men and women involved in the incident were detained and taken to the main station for investigation. The details are as follows:

Caught Stealing Fish

Yu Garden on Jiangwan Road is a private garden built by a Cantonese businessman named Deng. It has a fish pond where fish are raised and bred. This has attracted the covetousness of nearby villagers who often bring nets at night, climb over the fence, and steal fish. The garden caretaker, Yao Huaichuan from Xuzhou, was reprimanded by the garden owner. At around 9 PM last night, Yao discovered shadows moving in the fish pond, realizing that someone was stealing fish. He went to interfere. The villagers fled in a panic with their nets. Yao apprehended one person, Zhao Liansheng (17 years old) from Pudong, along with the nets. He called Gao Hehan, a police officer from the Jiangwan Road police station, intending to take him to the station for investigation. When they arrived at the garden gate, Chen Baozong (25 years old) from Jiading, who works as Chinese police officer No. 83 at Hongkou Park, suddenly interfered and spoke rudely. Officer Gao planned to take him to the station together.

Surrounded and Attacked En Route

As the group passed in front of 63 Garden, Wang Zhu Shi, the wife of Wang Abing, who runs a teahouse, gathered a crowd of over ten people carrying wooden sticks and rushed up to them, demanding that Officer Gao release Chen and Zhao. Officer Gao ignored them and was surrounded and attacked by the crowd, who tore his face and bruised his right [arm]. Yao was also injured on his fingers and face. Seeing the situation was unfavorable, Officer Gao blew his whistle. Police officers from nearby posts rushed over, and the crowd dispersed. Only the village woman Wang Zhu Shi was arrested, along with Chen Baozong and Zhao Liansheng, and taken to the North Station Branch for questioning. It is reported that the bureau believes Chen and the other three men and women dared to assault police officers, were involved in theft, and are truly hateful. They will be sent to the main bureau for further investigation.

Nanhui County Government Sued

The County Government Did Not Punish the Deceased’s Estate for Short Payment of Public Funds After the Death of the Tax Collection Clerk

Guarantor Suffers and Seeks Legal Relief

Zhang Xiang Sheng from Datianzhu Village outside the East Gate of Nanhui County, Pudong, acted as guarantor for the late Pu Yansheng, who served as a tax collection clerk in the 20th year of the Republic [1931]. According to regulations, a guarantee certificate was required. After Pu Yansheng died of illness, the Nanhui County Government calculated that Pu Yansheng was short 1,825 yuan in public funds and ordered Zhang to pay the compensation. Zhang argued that Pu Yansheng had land and property worth over 3,000 yuan, which was sufficient to cover the debt. He requested that the county government first dispose of the deceased Pu Yansheng's estate. If that was insufficient, the guarantor should then compensate for the remaining amount. However, the county government did not respond to his request and repeatedly sent officials to arrest Zhang Xiang Sheng and押交[unknown term], forcing Zhang to flee to Shanghai. He hired lawyer Yang Changchi to file a lawsuit with the Jiangsu High Court, seeking relief. The defendants are listed as the Nanhui County Government and Pu's heirs. The petition requests that the competent authorities be designated to hear the case. The High Court designated the Shanghai District Court to handle the case. Yesterday, Judge Han Jingdou opened the trial. Only Yang, Zhang's attorney, appeared in court. He stated that Zhang Xiang Sheng is 46 years old, from Nanhui, residing in Nanhui Sanguo Bajia. The plaintiff guaranteed that Pu Yansheng would act as a tax collection clerk in the 20th year of the Republic [1931], owing 1,825 yuan. However, the county government directly ordered the plaintiff to compensate. The principal debtor had 19.27 mu of land and 4.5 rooms, totaling over 3,000 yuan. The plaintiff repeatedly requested that the property of the principal debtor be disposed of first. However, the county government ignored this and insisted on arresting the plaintiff, violating Article 745 of the Civil Code. Therefore, the lawsuit requests that the Jiangsu High Court designate this court to hear the case. It also requests a judgment that Pu Yansheng's property be sealed and used to compensate first. If that is insufficient, the plaintiff will then supplement the amount. Finally, a declarative judgment is requested. The judge stated that the case requires investigation and ordered a future hearing.

Salmon Tax Evasion Case Verdict

Ye Zhenchang, owner of Zhenda Fish Firm; and Weng Zhaofang, shareholder and manager of Jieshun Salted Goods Firm in Xiaodongmen Xian Gua Street; and Zheng Yunsheng, manager of Shengji Salted Goods Firm in 16 Pu; along with Ye’s younger brother Ye Zhenqin and Zhang Benhua, were all reported by their colleagues Zhu Xusheng, Zhao Lianfang, and Chang Junfa to the Nanshi District Court last autumn. The report stated that Ye et al. had used fraudulent means to evade tariffs on over 6,700 dan of salmon shipped from Soviet Russia to Shanghai, with a tariff value of over 70,000 yuan, evading national taxes and violating serious laws. Fearing exposure and unforgiving judgment under law, they voluntarily surrendered themselves. Prosecutor Xiao investigated and found the accusations to be true, filing a public prosecution. Judge Wu Deying held numerous hearings, totaling over eight. Ye Zhenqin and Zhang Benhua avoided appearing and were ordered to be arrested. The defendants in court were thoroughly investigated, and arguments were concluded. Yesterday was the date of sentencing. The judge noted that the defendants are all reputable merchants who had accidentally violated the law, so the sentences were reduced. Ye Zhenchang was fined 1,000 yuan. Weng Zhaofang and Zheng Yuansheng were each fined 200 yuan. The informants Zhu Xusheng, Zhao Lianfang, and Chang Junfa were each reduced to a fine of 50 yuan, allowing them to reform. The trial against the fugitives Ye Zhenqin and Zhang Benhua was suspended until they are apprehended. After the verdict, the defendants' lawyers declared in court that they were dissatisfied. The judge stated that they could appeal according to the law after receiving the judgment.

Sentence for Trafficking Narcotics

Xu Shixun Sentenced to Twelve Years

The Puda Pharmaceutical Factory at 73, Lane 432, Avenue Petain, was opened by Yang Xinan (also known as Yang Jisheng) and specialized in producing and selling various pills and liquids containing potent narcotics. After testing by the Central Hygiene Experiment Institute in Nanjing, it was discovered that the medicines were adulterated with morphine. They confiscated products such as An Nao Bu Wan [Brain-Soothing Pills], Dwarf Gourd Essence, An Nao Bu Han [Brain-Soothing Sweating Pills], and Dwarf Gourd Pills. They were sent to the First Special Court. Xu was remanded in custody, and Yang was released on bail pending sentencing, as previously reported. The presiding judge Liu Yugui, because further investigation and evidence were needed, rescinded the conclusion of arguments. Yesterday morning, he presided over a further hearing in the Eighth Criminal Court. The defendants hired lawyers Chen Zhen and Shi Jiutang to defend them. Judge Liu announced the verdict in court: Xu Shixun is sentenced to twelve years in prison for continuously trafficking narcotics, and deprived of his civil rights for ten years. Yang Shouzhang is not guilty. Six boxes of Hundred-Supplement Holy Medicine, that is, Dwarf Gourd Pills, are confiscated and destroyed. The ledgers recording the Dwarf Gourd Pills are confiscated. The An Nao Wan, Dwarf Gourd Essence, and An Nao Juice, were examined by the Forensic Institute and found not to contain narcotics, and are to be returned.

Special District Rickshaw Pullers Association: General Meeting Held Yesterday

Discussion on Assisting the Municipal Council in Re-registering Rickshaw Pullers

After the rickshaw merchants in the Special District requested the registration of rickshaw pullers, the Municipal Council agreed to re-register them. The Council specifically stipulated the re-registration method: one rickshaw allows for the recommendation of one puller, three rickshaws allow for two pullers, and for those with a large number of rickshaws, one puller is allowed for every two rickshaws. The registration will begin on the 14th. The Special District Rickshaw Pullers Association held a general meeting of its members at its office at 3:00 PM yesterday. More than 90 people, including Gu Songmao, Hou Shao'an, Wang Kunyi, Lu Dexing, and Qiu Jixiang, attended. Gu Songmao chaired the meeting and first reported on the results of the negotiations with the Municipal Council after the previous strike. The Association received a written notice from the Rickshaw Committee regarding the registration method. After discussion, it was resolved that: All rickshaw owners must guide unemployed rickshaw pullers to register as soon as the re-registration begins; To ensure that all rickshaw owners are aware of the re-registration, the Association will send letters to summon the directors of the five districts (Southeast, Northwest) to notify them separately. The meeting adjourned at 7:00 PM. In addition, the Association sent a letter stating that Luo Jialun, president of National Central University, criticized the strike as inhumane to the rickshaw merchants. The Association clarified that it was forced to take such measures due to the Rickshaw Committee's repeated rent reductions and the difficulty of rickshaw pullers unwilling to pay mutual aid fees.

French Concession: Revised Method for Collecting House Tax

When the Rental Amount Includes Water, Electricity, or Equipment, the House Tax Can Be Appropriately Reduced Proportionately

The house tax levied by the French Concession Municipal Council is fixed at 13% of the rent. The tax is collected based on the rent receipts issued by the landlords. In the past, there were no deductions or reductions for the benefits enjoyed by the tenants. Recently, the Council prepared its budget for this year and revised the house tax calculation method. If the rent is used as the basis for the rental value, the total amount of house tax will be reduced in proportion to the amount of benefits enjoyed by the tenants, such as: Rent including water supply should be reduced by 5%; Rent including electricity supply should be reduced by 5%; Rent including garbage incineration equipment should be reduced by 5%; Rent including heating or cooling equipment should be reduced by 10%; Rent including elevator equipment should be reduced by 10%. However, the total reduction due to the above benefits cannot exceed 30% of the total rent. Regarding houses with equipment, the reduction method should be determined by the Director of the Finance Department of the Municipal Council or his representative, based on the scale of the equipment enjoyed by the tenants. However, this reduction cannot exceed 15% of the net value of the rent after the reduction for the benefits enjoyed by each tenant.

Strictly Prohibit Unscrupulous People from Excavating and Correct the County Government's Relocation Announcement

The Shenshi News Agency reported that Yu Hede, Chairman of the Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association in Shanghai, was concerned that the Yinxian County Government in Zhejiang Province had set a deadline for the demolition and relocation of all tombs in Ningbo City, causing the people to be at a loss. He telegraphed Huang Shaoxiong, Chairman of Zhejiang Province, and Zhao Cisheng, Commissioner of the Yinxian Administrative District, requesting them to consider the difficult situation and quickly correct the situation. The two telegrams are recorded below:

Telegram to Chairman Huang, Hangzhou, Zhejiang Province Chairman Huang Junjian, As reported, the Yinxian County Government announced that all existing tombs, floating coffins, and exposed coffins in the Ningbo city area must be demolished and relocated before May 10th. It is understood that the relocation of floating coffins and exposed coffins has long been implemented in Ningbo City. As for the existing tombs, there are registered regulations, and it is not appropriate to include them indiscriminately, which may cause disputes. In recent days, in rural areas outside the railway and provincial road areas, unscrupulous people have taken the opportunity to excavate tombs for profit, which is inhumane and has aroused public resentment. Therefore, we hereby request your Excellency to instruct the Yinxian County Magistrate to correct the hasty and inappropriate aspects of this announcement and order him to strictly prohibit excavation in rural areas to reassure the people. We await your reply. Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association, Yu Hede, et al., respectfully.

Telegram to Commissioner Zhao, Ningbo, Yinxian District Administrative Commissioner Zhao Xun, As reported, the Ningbo County Government announced that all tombs in the old city area of Ningbo, regardless of whether they are existing tombs, floating coffins, or exposed coffins, must be demolished and relocated before May 10th. The fellow villagers from the old city area in Shanghai are deeply alarmed and have come to the Association to inquire about the details and request assistance. It is understood that the demolition and relocation of floating coffins and exposed coffins has already been carried out in Ningbo, and those that have not been relocated are being registered by various townships and towns according to orders. Now, a sudden order has been issued to demolish and relocate the existing tombs as well, and the deadline is imminent, causing the people to be at a loss. In addition to reporting to Chairman Huang, we respectfully request you to consider the difficulty of demolishing and relocating existing tombs and quickly correct the announcement of the Yinxian County Government to reassure the people and avoid disputes. We await your reply. Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association, Yu Hede, et al., respectfully.

Old Woman Robbed, Injured, and Killed; Investigation Underway

Fire in Baliliqiao Street

Zhang Zhenxing rattan chair shop, located at No. 314 Baliliqiao Street outside Xiaobeimen in the French Concession, owned by Zhang Musheng, an old man from Pudong, had been in business for many years and was doing well. His three-story building was rented to Jiang Chuanyu, who operated a "Yang Emerald" workshop, specializing in the production of wooden combs, rings, and other ornaments, which were wholesaled to various shops for sale. Yesterday afternoon at 1:07 PM, the "Yang Emerald" workshop suddenly caught fire due to carelessness. Unexpectedly, the raw materials of "Yang Emerald" were all rosin and resin, which are difficult to extinguish once ignited. Thick smoke billowed, and flames raged. The patrol officers from the nearby police station immediately reported to the fire department by telephone. More than ten fire trucks rushed to the scene to pump water and extinguish the fire. The fire was extinguished after about an hour. As a result, the entire three-story building was burned down. Jiang Chuanyu, the owner of the fire, was arrested by the patrol officers and detained in the Songshan Road Police Station, to be sent to the Second Special District Court for investigation.

Miscellaneous News

Apprentice Attempts Suicide by Poisoning, Rescued. Dai Guobao, a 19-year-old apprentice from Shaoxing working at Tianhua Pharmaceutical Factory, No. 90 Gonghe Road, Zhabei, suddenly left without permission after dinner the day before yesterday. He did not return until dawn and secretly attempted suicide by poisoning. Fortunately, he was discovered early and immediately sent to Pushan Hospital for treatment. After examination, the doctor performed surgery and administered medication, causing him to vomit the poison and recover. According to the factory, two suicide notes were found in Dai's bedding and have been sent to the Xinzha Public Security Sub-bureau for record.

Four Bicycles Stolen. Zhixing Bicycle Shop, No. 1860 Bailinan Road, Huxi, was broken into by thieves at around 2:00 AM the night before last, and four bicycles were stolen. The next morning, the shop owner, Zhou Zhijin, 22 years old, from Nanxiang, discovered that his elder brother, Zhou Zhihao, was the thief. He reported to the Zhoujiaqiao Police Sub-station. Patrol Officer Wei Jiezhen dispatched police officer Wang Jinbang, accompanied by the shop owner, to search the attic of Zhou Zhihao's Zhitaiche shop at No. 1875 Bailinan Road. They recovered the four stolen bicycles and took Zhou Zhihao into custody, transferring him to the Caojiadu Public Security Sub-bureau for investigation.

Man's Body Found Hanging in Orchard. At around 4:00 PM the day before yesterday, an unidentified man's body was found hanging in the Xiwang Liantang orchard in Tuojiazhai, south of Xinlonghua, Huxi. The incident was reported to the Caoxing Police Station, which ordered Cao Yanchun, the local bailiff, to report to the local court. Yesterday, the court appointed prosecutor Xiao Jinying and coroner to conduct an on-site inspection. The deceased was found to be in his 30s, with a pockmarked face, wearing a gray felt hat, a black silk padded jacket, a Yuan-colored cloth shirt, a floral striped short shirt and undershirt, two pairs of blue cloth pants, a blue cloth apron, white socks, and moon-colored cloth shoes. He used a white belt to hang himself from a peach tree, kneeling on the ground. It was determined that he had died by suicide. Since no relatives were found, the court ordered photos to be taken and the body to be handed over to the bailiff for temporary burial, pending identification.

China Harmonica Society Records and Releases Harmonica Music

Since the establishment and promotion of harmonica music by the China Harmonica Society, it has become popular throughout the country. The harmonica is easy to learn, economical, noble, and offers a refreshing way to play with endless interest. Recently, the China Harmonica Society, in order to popularize music among the people, was invited by Asia Ersi Victory Company to record several new harmonica records, including the Society's harmonica team performing famous Chinese music such as "Battlefield Moon," "Happy Coppersmith March," and Society President Wang Qingxun's solo performances of "Lovebirds," "Flower of Kaga Island," "Merry Widow," and Chinese folk songs. They have now been produced and are being sold in record stores throughout the country. Those who study harmonica music and appreciate noble art can purchase them for reference.

The Ham Trade in Shanghai (Continued)

— Chief Editor of China Credit

(Part 21 of the Overview of Industry and Commerce in Shanghai) 2. Ham Merchants in the City

The ham merchants in the city are distinguished by their origins: Lanxi, Danyang, Ningbo, Zhenjiang, and Huizhou. Although the number of Jinlan and Lanxi ham merchants is small, they are purely ham merchants. The Ningbo, Zhenjiang, and Huizhou merchants also account for a small number. The Danyang merchants account for the largest number, accounting for 40-50% of the total. However, most of the Danyang merchants are frozen meat and cured meat shops that also sell hams, so they cannot be considered purely ham merchants. Before the September 18th Incident, there were more than 200 ham shops in Shanghai. Today, the number is much lower. Currently, there are only eight or nine relatively large ham shops in Shanghai. There used to be nine shops that formed a "Great United Association," but there is no distinction between large and small shops in the industry. However, these few shops are indeed larger in scope than others. A list of their names is provided below for reference.

Shop Name Address Manager's Name

Junfeng Henan Road, Paochengchang Zhan Zhiliang

Feng North Fujian Road Lou Renshou

South Wanyouquan East Men Road Cai Jiqing

North Wanyouquan Nanjing Road Dong Shaozhi

Jinlan Nanjing Road Guan Ruqing

Tongfeng East Men Road Wang Wuting

Maoshenghe Nanjing Road Wang Wuting

Tongshenghe Henan Road Wu Chushan

(Note) Tongfeng, Maoshenghe, and Ruishenghe are affiliated shops. Ham merchants used to jointly establish a Ham Industry Association, but since the production area of southern ham is Jinhua, the association was attached to the Jinhua Guildhall outside the West Gate. Since the establishment of the Ham Industry Association, the name of the association no longer exists. The current Ham Industry Association is located in Gongheli, Fuzhou Road, with a secretary stationed in the association to manage all association affairs. As for the association fees, they are not uniform for each shop. Large shops pay two yuan per month, medium shops pay one yuan per month, and small shops pay six jiao per month. The capital of ham merchants varies in size. If they set up their own buying stations in the production area to purchase goods, they must have capital of around 150,000 yuan. For medium-sized shops, 30,000 to 40,000 yuan is sufficient. For cured meat shops that also sell hams, the scale is even smaller, and a capital of several thousand yuan is enough to manage.

The ham business has gradually developed since 1929, and sales in various places have been very prosperous. If it can continue to develop, the future is limitless. Unexpectedly, after the September 18th Incident and the January 28th Shanghai Incident, the Shanghai market gradually declined, and sales in various places stagnated again. Harbin, Liaoning, and other places, which used to have large sales volumes, have now completely stopped trading. From May, June, July, and August last year, the ham market was at its lowest point. The selling price of northern ham in Shanghai fell to a minimum of 24-25 yuan per dan, which was a loss of 20 yuan per dan compared to the purchase cost (45-46 yuan per dan). This year, there has been a slight turnaround, and the selling price has risen to 33-34 yuan per dan (Shanghai scale). However, due to years of losses, production in the production area has decreased significantly. Southern ham can be sold after being stored for one or two years. Last year, the selling price in Shanghai was about 40 yuan per dan. This year, it has rebounded slightly to about 46-47 yuan. It is said that it is still difficult for ham merchants to make a profit, or that they still have to lose several yuan per dan. (The End)

Shanghai Residents' Spring Outing Extravaganza

Over 10,000 People Departed in the Past Two Days, Estimated Spending of 400,000 Yuan

(Special Dispatch from This Newspaper) Starting today, and especially with the designation of "next Monday (the 13th) as Tomb-Sweeping Day," coupled with the existing Easter holidays for Western employees of Shanghai's foreign firms, Chinese bank employees are also taking advantage of the tomb-sweeping holiday. Drawing from past experience, many Chinese and foreign individuals in Shanghai are bound to travel. Returning home to sweep the tombs is a duty incumbent upon all children, especially as it coincides with the pleasantly mild weather following the Qingming Festival. This year's wave of tourists is even more enthusiastic than in previous years, stemming from the interconnected nature of bank holidays and tomb-sweeping outings, a truly perfect and legitimate combination. However, besides the banking sector, other institutions are not granting holidays, leaving some with tombs they cannot sweep. Can those who are children of their parents feel at ease?

Enough with the digressions. To investigate the number of people traveling in these two days, this reporter made inquiries at travel agencies and transportation companies, gaining a general understanding. First, regarding travel destinations, it is said that due to the short holiday, long-distance trips are rare. Hangzhou is the most popular destination, followed by Jinhua and Lanxi, then Suzhou and Wuxi, and finally Huangshan and Tianmu Mountain. Moganshan is mostly frequented by foreigners. Second, concerning the number of people, excluding previous days, in the past two days alone, over 10,000 people went to Hangzhou, 500 to Jinhua and Lanxi, about 400 to Suzhou, 300 to Wuxi, 100 to Huangshan, about 80 to Tianmu Mountain, and about 50 to Moganshan, totaling over 11,000 people. Third, regarding estimated expenses, naturally, wealthy individuals or families who go to Hangzhou to burn incense may spend hundreds of yuan without a second thought. Now, if we calculate an average of 35 yuan per person, the travel expenses for these 11,000 people amount to approximately 400,000 yuan.

The above figures pertain to those traveling by train. The exact number of people driving along the Shanghai-Hangzhou highway in private cars is difficult to ascertain at this time.

As for water travel, the Nanking Excursion Trip organized by Jardine Matheson departed last night on the "Gonghe" steamship. Although the Yangtze River is filled with muddy yellow water, the leisurely journey offers a sufficient opportunity to soak in the scenery of the water and sky. In addition, many people are traveling to Ningbo by boat to visit Xuedou Temple. Furthermore, Sir. F.Lirth-Ross has also organized a tour group to Ningbo, departing on the "New Beijing."

The reporter also visited the North Railway Station and found it bustling with activity. Automobiles formed rows in the square, fashionable women resembled clouds in the hall, and the platforms were filled with clusters of people. Each person wore a satisfied smile, holding cameras and binoculars. Women wore brightly colored new clothes, and children jumped around, creating an atmosphere of peace and prosperity. Although yesterday's weather was a bit chilly, it was much more refreshing than the sultry heat of the previous few days due to low pressure.

Those with the highest spirits were none other than the Hangzhou innkeepers and small boat operators. High-end hotels around the Inner Lake, such as the Xiling Hotel and the Xin Xin Hotel, had all their rooms booked in advance. Yesterday afternoon, many people were making long-distance calls to Hangzhou to reserve rooms, only to find it was already too late. As for the small boats in Hangzhou, they are sure to "shave the cucumbers," demanding no less than four yuan in legal tender for a day of rowing.

Shanghai residents are always enthusiastic about spending, with 400,000 yuan in travel expenses being spent in just three or four days. However, the city of Hangzhou, renowned worldwide for its scenery, expresses extreme delight.
