Education News

Ministry of Education Issues Revised High School Mathematics Curriculum Standards (Part Two)

Three, Third Academic Year

(I) Algebra (For Group A, continued from before): Complex Numbers, A. Properties and Four Operations, Polar Coordinates, B. De Moivre's Theorem, Roots of Complex Numbers; Equation Theory, A. General Properties of Equations, Relationship between Roots and Coefficients, Symmetric Functions of Roots, B. Transformations of Equations, Remainder Theorem for Rational Integral Functions, Separation of Roots, C. Approximate Methods for Finding Irrational Roots (Horner's and Newton's Methods); Determinants, A. Theorems and Properties, B. Expansion by Minors, C. Method of Elimination and Its Applications; Infinite Series, A. Convergence and Divergence, Principal Tests for Convergence of Various Series, B. Convergence of Σ 1/n^s Series, Study of Important Power Series, C. Approximate Value of Sum, D. Recurring Series, Infinite Products; Combinatorial Analysis, A. Binomial Theorem (with Mathematical Induction), B. Permutations and Combinations, C. Probability and Its Applications; Infinite Continued Fractions. (II) Analytic Geometry (Not used for Group B from the following downward): Cartesian Coordinates, A. Projection Theorem, B. Analytic Representation of Geometric Quantities (Angle, Distance, Area, Slope, Point of Division, etc.); Locus and Equation, A. Fundamental Theorems Concerning the Relationship between Locus and Equation, B. Variations and Graphical Representation of Algebraic and Transcendental Functions; First-Degree Equations - Straight Lines, A. Various Forms of Linear Equations and Families of Lines, B. Perpendicular Distance and Angle between Two Lines; Second-Degree Equations - Conic Sections, A. Equation and Properties of the Circle, B. Equation and Properties of the Ellipse, Parabola, and Hyperbola, D. Families of Conic Sections; Transformation of Coordinate Axes, A. Parallel Translation, B. Rotation; Relationship between Straight Lines and Conic Sections, A. Tangents and Normals, B. Asymptotes, C. Center and Diameter of Conic Sections; General Second-Degree Equation, A. Classification Conditions for Quadratic Curves, B. Degenerate Families of Conic Sections; Polar Coordinates, A. Polar Equations and Their Graphs for Various Loci, B. Conversion with Cartesian Coordinates; Equations with Three Variables and Higher-Order Plane Curves; Inversion of Conic Sections; Poles and Polars; Space Coordinates and Loci, A. Orthogonal Projection, Direction Cosines, B. Analytic Representation of Geometric Quantities, C. Equations of Planes and Lines; Planes and Lines, A. Various Equations of Planes and Lines, B. Relationship between Planes and Lines; Special Surfaces, A. Sphere, Cylinder, and Cone, B. Surface of Revolution and Ruled Surface; Transformation of Space Coordinate Axes; Quadric Surfaces, A. Discussion and Graphs of Equations of Quadric Surfaces, B. Relationship between Quadric Surfaces and Planes/Lines; Equations and Properties of Space Curves.

Four, Summary of Implementation Methods

Operational Requirements

The methods for classroom exercises, extracurricular exercises, and examinations are the same as those for junior high school. However, high school students have a more ample understanding ability and should have their interest in independent study stimulated and their ability to conduct independent research cultivated. Therefore, attention should be paid to the following matters: Designate teaching materials in advance and have students preview them. For simpler materials, students can be assigned to ask and answer questions in the classroom in lieu of didactic explanations. After studying a chapter or a substantial section, students should be required to create their own summaries in the form of tables or diagrams. Reference materials should be designated, and students should be directed to conduct group or individual independent consultations under the guidance of teachers, reporting the general outline of the results obtained or creating difficult problems outside the textbook for independent calculation and discussion. If it is not possible for all students in the class to complete this extracurricular assignment, it should be done by those with better aptitude and academic ability. In addition to lecturing on the regular curriculum, if there is extra time, students can practice their note-taking skills in the classroom, and then organize and transcribe their notes for the teacher to evaluate. Special teaching materials such as the following should be added: computational practice with compasses, theodolites, and levels; methods for calculating the range of guns and cannons; determination of angles of depression and angles of deflection in ordinary and military surveying; measurement of the angle of elevation of a gun; calculations of transportation and consumption; and methods for various investigations and statistics.

Two, Teaching Method Key Points

From the second academic year onward, this curriculum is taught in two groups, A and B. In addition to carefully teaching according to the teaching material outline, teachers must also pay attention to the following: (I) General Remarks: The high school curriculum is the second circumference of the junior high school curriculum, so there should be a practical connection between the two. The initial portion of the high school mathematics curriculum is the same as the junior high school teaching material. It is appropriate to select more difficult problems for review and to introduce deeper studies from there. Junior high school mathematics focuses on the mastery of calculation skills and understanding of basic concepts. The method of study is to induce general rules from examples and special cases. High school, on the other hand, should focus on the theoretical aspects, using the deductive method to conduct a more systematic study. Due to the complexity and depth of mathematical principles, junior high school students may not fully understand them. Therefore, the junior high school teaching material should still be reiterated in high school, but with different details, emphasis, and interests, so as not to bore students and to have the advantages of reviewing the old and knowing the new, and stripping away the silk. (II) Trigonometry: High school trigonometry should be centered on trigonometric functions. Acute-angle trigonometric functions and the solution of right triangles have already been studied in junior high school, so high school can start with general-angle trigonometric functions for comparison and demonstration of generalization. This is not only seeking the universality of theory but is also a necessary knowledge for those studying physics. The trigonometry taught in junior high school is primarily simple, while high school should pay attention to the properties of trigonometric functions, trigonometric identities, and equations (all of which should be compared with corresponding problems in algebra) for use when conducting higher mathematics. (III) Geometry: High school geometry should train students' ability to automatically explore and pay attention to logical order, so as to achieve a considerable degree of rigor. Geometry places the most emphasis on logical order. Junior high school students are young and immature, and it is not easy to strictly adhere to it. High school geometry teaching should pay special attention to this training, but the degree of theoretical rigor should be limited to what students can feel is necessary and can understand. The theorems already learned in junior high school should be dissected again using an enlightening method, and the method of proof by contradiction should be used as much as possible to clarify the path of thinking. The relationships between theorems should be used to form a system, showing the consistent thread of the entire geometry, so that students can grasp the key points and increase their ability to apply them. However, the system should be viewed from a theoretical perspective to facilitate understanding and memory and should not be reduced to rigid classification. Parts that were not taught in detail in junior high school should be supplemented, and attention should be paid to the two parts of loci and construction problems. In addition to reasoning and proving problems, these two parts can also develop students' ability to explore and invent. Geometric proofs and constructions should use algebraic methods as much as possible within the possible scope to find the relationship between known and unknown quantities. Solid geometry focuses on clarifying spatial properties and measurement methods, so that students can see through the figures on the plane and understand the structure of various solids in order to connect with the drawing of utensils in the drawing class. (IV) Algebra and Higher Algebra: High school algebra should focus on functions and equations. Students do not easily understand the concept of function. Teachers should explain it carefully when deriving the variations of elementary functions to establish its foundation. The quadratic function is the most suitable example. Junior high school graduates can understand the method of solving equations, so high school algebra should focus on the general properties of equations, the principle of co-solution, discussing the changes in solutions ("equations containing parameters") and increasing or decreasing ("such as the roots of fractional equations and irrational equations"). The quadratic equation is the entry point to equations and is most suitable for training students' thinking. Higher algebra focuses on equation theory. The existence of complex numbers is a prerequisite for the establishment of the fundamental theorem of algebra. Determinants are a powerful tool for the elimination method. Although series are limit operations and differ greatly from algebraic properties, all expansions of functions rely on them and are the foundation of analytic geometry. Therefore, more attention should also be paid to them. Application problems of equations should not be limited to daily facts but should be connected with geometry, trigonometry, physics, and chemistry. In practical problems, attention should be paid to the accuracy of the results obtained. Numerical solution methods for higher-degree numerical equations have many practical uses and should be known by those who study calculation. Probability is the core of statistics and should also be taught in general terms. (V) Analytic Geometry: High school analytic geometry should integrate algebra, geometry, and trigonometry to show the mutual use of these subjects. On the one hand, it serves as a general conclusion to the mathematics subjects in the middle school stage, and on the other hand, it establishes the foundation for higher-level research. Analytic geometry should be connected with algebra, geometry, and trigonometry to solve geometric problems and to fully express the interconnected nature of the various parts of mathematics. To make the figure and quantity correspond to each other, it is necessary to use generalized geometric elements, so analytic geometry cannot but differ from synthetic geometry (such as the problem of finding the angle bisector). In all such places, it is best to make beginners pay attention to clarify their understanding and avoid confusion. If there is sufficient time, the meaning of Impossible Construction should be briefly indicated. (End)

Ministry of Education Circular: Advocate for Anti-Drug Education

The Ministry of Education issued a circular on the 8th to the education bureaus of various provinces and cities, stating, "Approved is the public letter No. 343 on Prohibition Policy, dated February 29th, of the 25th year [of the Republic], from the Anti-Smoking Committee of the National Government Military Commission. The letter states, 'Upon review of the proposal by Committee Member Zhong Ketuo at the Committee's first regular meeting, to promote the public's anti-drug movement to facilitate a two-year drug prohibition and six-year opium suppression policy, and the proposals by Committee Member Ma Liang and Committee Member Ma Pingchen, to promote anti-drug education and anti-smoking propaganda, and to utilize social moral sanctions to enhance the power of political laws, so as to achieve rapid results, the matter was discussed jointly and resolved to send a letter to the Central Party Headquarters and the Ministry of Education for reference and implementation, to arouse the public's correct understanding of the government's determination to prohibit smoking, its policies, and methods, so as to unite all levels and jointly resist drugs. The records are on file. This Committee deeply believes that drug and opium prohibition is the most important task of the government, has already issued general orders to the entire country to comply, and is also a point of extreme attention for friendly countries. The deadline is pressing, and the laws are strict, allowing no pretense. However, most of the people in various places who smoke opium and other drugs are ignorant and unknowing, and easily fall into the legal net. It is imperative to widely disseminate information to persuade and guide them, to show the intention of not punishing them without first educating them. Accordingly, the instructions of the Chairman of the Military Commission and Concurrent Supervisor of Drug Prohibition and the declarations and announcements of this Committee are enclosed herewith and forwarded to you. Please examine them for reference. We urge the Ministry of Education to adopt Committee Member Ma's proposal to promote anti-drug education and to instruct its affiliated provincial and municipal education bureaus and schools at all levels to expand propaganda, so as to achieve practical results and complete the task.' The above is approved. The matter concerns the important policy of opium prohibition and should be handled accordingly. In addition to replying and issuing separate orders, we are forwarding the enclosed printed materials, ordering your department to comply immediately and to instruct all affiliated departments to comply accordingly. This order."

Ministry of Education, Today's Educational Broadcast Program

Topic: National Finance and Currency

Lecturer: Ma Yinchu

Time: 6:00 PM to 6:30 PM

Frequency: 660 (Central Broadcasting Station)

Broadcasting Organization: People's Education Center

Chinese Economic Society: This Year's Annual Meeting to Be Held in Shanghai

The Chinese Economic Society was founded in the old capital during the 12th year of the Republic [1923]. Subsequently, it expanded annually, establishing branches in Beiping, Tianjin, Shanghai, Hangzhou, Changsha, and Guangzhou. The headquarters were relocated to the capital, and plans were made to build a society building and library. After the last annual meeting was held in Guangzhou and a portion of the directors were re-elected, the current board of directors convened its inaugural meeting in January, mutually electing a president and vice president. As a result, Mr. Li Zhaohuan was elected president, and Mr. Ma Yinchu was elected vice president. Secretary Wu Xiaoyuan resigned, and Cao Lishun was recommended to succeed him. Ten Important Aspects of Vocational Supplementary Education (II)

— Jiang Wenyu

The above was said from the perspective of the youth's parents and elder brothers. Let's talk about it from the perspective of the youth themselves. After graduating from elementary school, they cannot enter middle school because of poverty. After graduating from middle school, they cannot enter university because of poverty. Helpless, they have to go to factories and shops to be apprentices and workers. They see a group of classmates who graduated at the same time, whose grades are not as good as theirs, but because their parents and elder brothers are rich, they can enjoy the happiness of further education. Looking at themselves, they are just sinking into the industrial and commercial world as an apprentice or a low-level clerk. Thus, the more they think about it, the more unfair and uncomfortable they feel. Isn't this a real situation in society? Do not underestimate this situation! You must know that the youth's frustration and depression have a very significant impact on society. If there is vocational supplementary education, this problem can also be solved. They can work on one hand and go to school on the other, which is very convenient. Those with elementary school diplomas can enter supplementary schools equivalent to junior high schools. Those with junior high school diplomas can enter supplementary schools equivalent to senior high schools. Those with senior high school diplomas can enter supplementary schools equivalent to specialized schools. They can take a longer time to learn step by step and complete the studies they want to pursue. Furthermore, learning in this kind of supplementary school is more practical than being a formal student in a formal school because they come to learn out of need. Then, the individual's goal of further education is achieved, the vocational skills are especially enhanced, and the status of the occupation is gradually improved. All the frustration and discontent of the youth in society are completely eliminated. Tell me, isn't this kind of education important? This is seeing the importance of vocational supplementary education from the perspective of the youth who cannot continue their education.

(V)

Let's talk about ordinary students. Do middle school graduates who do not go on to further education have jobs to do? Not necessarily. Should university graduates get a job? Not necessarily. Shouldn't vocational school graduates have something to do? Still not necessarily. Then, what is so valuable about graduating and going on to further education? But is it okay not to go to school? That is also not okay. What should we do then? I think the best way is to have young people enter the workforce after receiving national education, and then enter vocational supplementary schools (this of course refers to vocational supplementary schools above the secondary level). This is more appropriate. Of course, national elementary schools are compulsory education, which should be popularized. That goes without saying. As for the establishment of junior high schools and senior high schools for those preparing for further education, vocational schools for those preparing to enter the workforce, and normal schools for those preparing to teach, how to establish them, how many to establish, how to study, and how many students to enroll, we can temporarily leave aside and let others seek reasonable measures. We now focus on hoping for the establishment of a large number of vocational supplementary schools to meet the needs of young people who have already entered the workforce after graduating from elementary school. We believe that young people who enter the workforce should attend supplementary schools. This is not only their right but also their obligation. We must shift the general social perception to recognize that young people who have a job and then enter supplementary school are very valuable and very respectable. Conversely, those who enter useless universities, do not learn any skills, and just wear a square hat are not necessarily useful. In this way, the value of vocational supplementary education will immediately increase. This is seeing the importance of vocational supplementary education from the perspective of the career paths of graduates.

(VI)

Let's talk about education policy. May I ask, when a country runs education, is it hoping that it can help improve society, and that it can help improve social industries? Scientific education and applied scientific education in universities and specialized schools are, of course, the foundation for establishing and improving industries. Formal vocational school education is to train the majority of workers who improve industries. However, the number of universities and specialized schools is limited, and how many people can enter formal vocational schools? We hope that this kind of education that helps improve industries can truly be popularized in society and show great effectiveness. Then, vocational supplementary education is probably the best tool. Because it can enable all young people and adults in the entire industry to receive appropriate training and increase their production skills. May I ask, should this kind of education be promoted? Should it be designated as the country's most important education policy? This is seeing the importance of vocational supplementary education from the perspective of national education policy.

In terms of educational effectiveness, we should certainly recognize that vocational supplementary education is very important. Even in terms of improving the nation's industries and increasing the nation's wealth, we must especially plan for the promotion of vocational supplementary education. Let's imagine that a country has tens of thousands of young people and adults who work in farms, factories, and commercial places during the day, helping the country and society produce, and in the morning and evening, they study vocational skills, so that their production and work efficiency is greatly improved. How great is this kind of effect? If it is not like this, then how can production efficiency be increased? If there are only senior technical talents, but no mid-level and low-level workers who have received appropriate training to be used, I am afraid it is still useless. From this, we can prove the value and importance of vocational supplementary education. This is seeing the importance of vocational supplementary education from the perspective of increasing production efficiency.

Let's talk about vocational education itself. Vocational education was originally based on formal agricultural, industrial, and commercial vocational schools as the orthodox path. However, now it is not the case. In addition to formal vocational schools, there are also vocational supplementary schools and vocational guidance. It can be said that the entire composition of vocational education has these three elements, just like the three legs of a tripod, none of which can be missing. Because vocational schools alone can never popularize vocational education. With vocational schools, and then with vocational supplementary schools, then vocational education can be said to be popularized. This is a certain and unchangeable principle. Formal vocational schools require formal equipment and formal students. Of course, students do nothing else but study. Not to mention today's China, vocational schools cannot be universally established. Even in Europe and America, how can they be universally established? Moreover, whether vocational school graduates have jobs to take after leaving school depends on the social situation. If the vocational supplementary school admits people who are already working in the industry, it is of course much more convenient and these problems will not occur. This can really supplement the lack of effectiveness of formal vocational schools and make the effectiveness of vocational education universal in society. This is seeing the importance of vocational supplementary education from the perspective of the effectiveness of vocational education itself.

School Investigation - An Overview of British Schools in Shanghai (I) by Hu Zuyin

There are a total of seven British schools in Shanghai; five public schools are the Municipal Council Western Public Schools established by the Public Concession; and two private schools are English Boys' and Girls' Schools established by British expatriates. The five Western Public Schools established by the Municipal Council admit the children of Westerners who pay taxes in the Public Concession. Therefore, although the training and educational facilities in the schools are mainly based on British educational principles, they also take into account the children of expatriates from other countries, and cannot implement purely British-style education. However, since the students enrolled in private English schools are all children of British expatriates, and their organization and management are all managed by British expatriates in Shanghai, all facilities in the schools can represent the characteristics of purely British education. This article first describes the overview of the private English boys' school; the overview of the private English girls' school will be introduced in another article later. The author is very grateful to Reverend Quake, the principal of the school, for providing information in many ways and for providing a booklet about the school!

1. A School Representing British Education

The original name of the private English boys' school was The Cathedral Boys School, Henry Lester Endowment, which directly translates to the Cathedral Boys' School established by the Lester Heritage Fund. Originally, the school was initially established in 1902 by Holy Trinity Church (Editor's note: a cathedral is the chapel where the bishop resides) at No. 219 Jiangxi Road; the purpose of establishing the school at that time was to recruit children for the cathedral choir. Later, the number of children enrolled gradually increased, and the school became a school for British children. However, the school buildings initially built were not suitable for educational ideals; therefore, the wealthy British merchant Mr. Lester bequeathed a large sum of money to the school in his will to rebuild the new school buildings when he was dying. At that time, Holy Trinity Cathedral was willing to lease a piece of land to the school for the construction of school buildings, so the school had a source of land and funding. In September 1929, the new school buildings were completed, and the number of students increased. The school officially became an English boys' school.

The school was established for two purposes: the first is to prepare British children to enter public middle schools in their home country when they return home; the second is to provide children who do not return to their home country with an education in Shanghai similar to that of British public middle schools. Mr. Lester stipulated in his will that students at the school must be British citizens, be at least seven years old, and have a clear background. The school is organized into two years of preparatory courses and six years of middle school. The preparatory course is equivalent to our country's higher elementary school, and the middle school is divided into junior and senior levels, with two years in the junior level and four years in the senior level. Graduates of the school can participate in the entrance examination held in Shanghai by Cambridge University in the United Kingdom; if they pass the examination, they can directly enter famous universities in the United Kingdom without examination. The school tries its best to assimilate with British schools in terms of training and educational facilities and atmosphere; the teachers and staff employed are all graduates from British universities to implement this British-style education.

As the End of the Fourth Month Approaches, the Financial Situation Still Feels Sluggish

In past years, during the long flood season, deposits and withdrawals in the banking and money industries were extremely busy. However, this year, everything has come to a standstill. Moreover, long-term loans from Ningbo also cannot be transferred, and almost all must be settled. In order to avoid danger and ensure their own safety, banks and money shops can hardly take care of everything. Although long-term settlements yesterday were only a little over 300,000, the amount that needs to be settled in the recent few days is no less than ten million. It is unknown how to resolve this. The interbank loan rate remains at 8%. In the interbank bill market, morning transactions involved over 3.4 million in transfers and over 400,000 in new transactions. Afternoon transactions involved over 700,000. Transactions in the Small General Association amounted to over 500,000. Repurchases of foreign collateral loans amounted to over 700,000, and new loans made amounted to over 200,000. According to insiders, major banks have slightly agreed to lend over 1 million in credit. Issues amounted to over 1.7 million locally and over 300,000 elsewhere. Money shops received over 42.2 million in foreign public bills and over 3.4 million in foreign head loans. Remittances from various sources amounted to over 400,000. New Measures for Export Tea Inspection This Year (Continued)

(4) Let's talk about colored tea. The export of colored tea should have been strictly prohibited. Since the United States issued the Colored Tea Prohibition Ordinance in 1911, Japanese tea has been able to sell well in the United States due to the negligence of Chinese tea merchants. In 1932, French Africa also advocated prohibiting the import of toxic colored tea. Although the local government has not implemented it, because it is tea eaten by the natives, the colonial government is naturally unwilling to implement it strictly, but it is also very dangerous. Recently, the French government has been actively researching tea in Annam, which is clear evidence. Russia is the largest customer for Chinese tea. In recent years, they have also purchased Japanese tea as a substitute because Chinese tea is colored. The Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry has determined that the history of colored tea is too long and the sales are too wide, and at the request of tea merchants, a gradual ban method was set. The highest standards for three different colors of colored tea concentration are set each year. All exported colored tea with the same or darker color as the standard is prohibited from export. In this way, the concentration of colored tea can be reduced year by year. In order to take care of the difficulty of tea merchants in selecting non-toxic yellow coloring materials, officials were assigned to specialize in the research of tea-use non-yellow coloring materials. In the 23rd year, eight types of improved non-toxic yellow coloring materials were invented. After the Shanghai Foreign Tea Trade Association and the Shanghai Tea Industry Association were satisfied with the trial use, the Tea Industry Association funded the establishment of a factory to manufacture improved coloring materials. Because the raw materials are fine, the cost is relatively large, and the selling price is inevitably higher than that of toxic coloring materials. However, the strength is strong, and the amount used is less than that of toxic coloring materials. In comparison, using improved coloring materials is more economical than using toxic coloring materials. However, workers in tea shops in various places have not been accustomed to using it, so they lack confidence in manufacturing. From this year onwards, a new type of "No. 10 Yellow" has been made, which is more advanced than the previous types. Last month, the bureau invited tea merchants to discuss and decide on several methods.

A. Shanghai, Wenzhou, and Pingshui stipulate that each household must have at least one dan, Tunxi Yushan must have at least half a dan, and Wuyuan Suian must have at least 20 jin. Except for Yushan, which is directly sent by the bureau to the county government to order tea shops to purchase it, the rest of the places are distributed to each household by the tea shops for trial use. If there are still any unsatisfactory aspects of the trial use, the tea shops or tea houses can directly send a letter to the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau for improvement.

B. Each tea shop should be responsible for supervising each tea house to purchase and use it, and the bureau will send personnel to various places to investigate and guide at any time.

In the future, if tea merchants do not use improved pigments, they will be prohibited from exporting once they are inspected. If the colored tea cannot be exported, no one will care about domestic sales. Isn't the loss of tea merchants very big?

(5) Regarding the tea box issue: There is another brochure that explains why we want to reform and ban inferior tea boxes, which can be consulted. I won’t say more here, but there are two points that should be paid special attention to for manufacturing improved tea boxes.

1. The four triangular wooden strips at the locking point of the tea box are best nailed on after the lead cylinder is put in. If the tenon joint at each end can be made slightly flat, it will be more suitable when nailed together. Otherwise, it doesn't matter much.

2. Because the improved tea boxes now have triangular wooden strips on each side, the old lead cans are not easy to put in very tightly. In the future, the newly made lead cans should be changed to curved or rounded edges so that the lead cans and the entire box can be tightly attached. Not only is there no gap, but the amount of tea loaded will not be reduced. According to our calculations, it will only reduce about one catty compared to the original amount of tea per box.

In addition, if tea merchants in various places have any unclear or difficult questions, they may send a letter to inquire, and we will wholeheartedly answer them. (Omitted below) (End)

Shen Bao Literary Special Issue

Feminine Perspectives in Modern Literature

— Xu Chen

(I)

Let's take a look at how women are portrayed in modern world literature.

First, we must talk about Madame Hulot in Balzac's "Cousin Bette."

As everyone knows, "Cousin Bette" depicts the decadent aristocratic life of the so-called Duke Hulot, gradually declining under the pressure of the emerging bourgeois forces of the time. It portrays the demise of the aristocracy and the rise of the bourgeoisie—a historical masterpiece of Balzac's depiction of the class society of France at that time.

Engels regarded Balzac's success as Balzac's realism. Indeed, Balzac accurately observed the reality of society at that time, so he concretely depicted historical truth. But what kind of person is Madame Hulot who emerges from Balzac's "realism"? This lady is portrayed as lacking her own opinions, full of religious enthusiasm, and not resisting the ugliness of this world but hoping for the afterlife, a kind of "saint" of the present world. Balzac portrayed her through his own subjectivity—that is, by pursuing such a woman as his ideal woman.

We can place Balzac's ideal woman in Madame Hulot. We can also imagine that such a woman was real among the dying French aristocracy. Then, perhaps this is a woman who is depicted as a symbol of the dying aristocratic class, to be mourned.

Balzac, who completely depicted the typical and stood on the side of the emerging class, not only in his new revolutionary nature, but also in his view of women, took the idealization of the feudalism of the old era—a saint who is cleansed of all worldly sins—as the requirement for women. Therefore, judging from Madame Hulot, Balzac never saw the new woman, nor could he become a friend of the future of women's liberation.

(II)

After Balzac, the writers of the peak of naturalism included Zola, Flaubert, and Maupassant. Zola wrote about Nana in "Nana", Flaubert wrote about Madame Bovary in "Madame Bovary"; Maupassant wrote about Jeanne in "A Woman's Life." When these women are viewed outside of the historical evaluation of their works, it can be said that they are not only depicted as a biological side. Of course, people are biological; one cannot talk about depicting the foundation of humans without depicting them as biological beings. But at the same time, humans are also social animals. The history of mankind is the process of human effort to establish "oneself as a social being" from "oneself as a biological being."

Someone once said: "History is the effort of humans to return from 'nature in humans' to 'humans in humans'." This means: humans temper the "human" natural attributes (biological instincts) into "humans in humans" (cultural, social nature; humanity.)—This kind of effort is the historical essence of human society. Therefore, the true posture of a human being is a unity mixed with biological elements and social human elements.

Therefore, when a writer begins to describe the posture of a person, if they only focus on the biological side, they have not described half of the human being, and they have not seen the human social connection and life development.

The basic ideology of naturalistic literature is materialism that stops at "the discovery of biological humans." Therefore, the above-mentioned writers of that era did not primarily focus on biological humans. This can be said to be a major revolution from the previous method, but it is still not enough in modern times (present).

Understanding this point and then savoring naturalistic literature can reveal a good lesson: that is, the tragedy of Nana or Jeanne is the tragedy of "people not pursuing human cultural things in life."

(III)

In naturalistic literature, only in the works of Ibsen and Bjørnson is there a tendency to demand and advocate the restoration of women's human rights—freedom of love, marriage, divorce, etc.—putting this idea of women's liberation into the works and singing it out. Ibsen's "A Doll's House" and "The Lady from the Sea" and Bjørnson's "A Gauntlet," etc., are well known to everyone. But in these works, only revolutionary advocacy of women's freedom of love and marriage can be seen; the authors did not think about political and economic freedom.

Anyone who knows the names of female characters such as Nora, Ellida, and Svava can understand this. At that time in Europe, resistance of the people against capitalism—demands for economic and political liberation—had already begun. From this point of view, Ibsen and Bjørnson's ideas of women's liberation are only a kind of petty-bourgeois revolutionary thought.

A German critic named Ellen Key once criticized it this way.

In short, Ibsen's thought is a true voice for a part of women's lack of rights; but he still did not understand that "women must have economic and political liberation first if they truly want this kind of freedom." Therefore, Ibsen's plays soon lost their appeal to the masses.

To put it plainly: Ibsen said in his works that women must be given freedom of love and freedom of personality, but how to give it? Even if it is given like Nora, and she walks out into society, can society guarantee that freedom? If it is to be guaranteed, what method should be used?… Ibsen did not answer these subsequent questions, so the result was the loss of the importance of the women's issue.

No Spring

— Plum Rain

Not a single budding flower,

Not a single golden phoenix flower.

Like our past years,

There is no spring!

There is no spring—

On the bloody front line,

In the barren fields,

Before the rumbling machine,

On the noisy roadside sandwiched by gray buildings,

Unemployed wanderers,

Pitiable smiling sellers,

Like homeless sick dogs,

Trembling in the cold wind.

Let the heroes of the times

Put on the wings of battle,

And take back our spring!

Fisherman

— Lin Na

(Philippines, an island with no seasons.)

The land on the equator is forever growing in melancholy. The evening breeze that shakes rose fragrance in the coconut grove brings a relaxing dusk.

It has been three days without seeing the season of spring. The old fisherman, Simon Ding, has returned from the beach in disappointment. His heavy footsteps woke me from my tired sleep. I gently opened my eyes and saw a thick layer of darkness smeared in the thatched hut, and I was secretly surprised: "Damn! Why did it get dark as soon as I closed my eyes?" So I climbed down from the wooden frame and ran out the door.

A salty, fishy wind blew from the seaside, making people unable to help but shiver gently. The afterglow of the setting sun had also turned into a faint smear, floating on the distant water ripples.

At this time, Lina, a beautiful and melancholy girl in the fishing village, with her head lowered, was immersed in deep thought, and walked lightly out of the opposite coconut grove. Her strong back silently brought a burst of sad singing

"...Youth is like a beautiful flower, girl! Please do not fail this, fail this beautiful night..."

Then there was a sharp whistle and a high-pitched laughter. However, this is irrelevant to me: a young fisherman; so I walked back to the house again. The thatched hut was already dilapidated, damp and narrow. The old man Simon Ding sat silently on a wooden stool with a lame leg, silently thinking about his precious memories: his wife, children, house and耕牛 that have been separated for three years and are still lost in the deep mountains and forests...

He has a big wish: to build his ideal giant house and three decent bulls in the mountains of Rizal Province. It was he who encouraged him to leave his wife and children from his distant hometown to come here, and it was he who made him feel excited and lifted the fishing net high when he was tired; however, the general depression and the rampant famine in the colony shattered his hopes, and he is now in debt. The bakery had long since declared to him; no more credit! Thinking of this, the melancholy and disappointed old man could not help but sigh sadly, his voice so desperate and sad. …

"You are a star in people's hearts, a beautiful lamp!..." The low singing vibrated again in the dark coconut grove.

The old man Simon Ding suddenly seemed to remember something, and he raised his head and wanted to shout loudly at the door: "Xi Ning!" But he saw me standing in front of him blankly, so he said in an irritable and reproachful tone:

"Are you crazy, why don't you turn on the lights at this time!"

"There's no coconut oil!" I replied lazily, my eyes still staring at him.

"Then what about the bread!" He shouted anxiously, but his tone seemed so weak and powerless.

"The bakery has long said that it won't give credit!..."

The old man raised his head and looked at the sky filled with night, and sighed again for a long time, painfully burying his disheveled head in his thin palms and remained silent.

The full moon was floating heavily on the edge of the vast sea, and the night was as soft and quiet as the waveless autumn water. …

A few bursts of enthusiastic laughter were embedded on the tips of the coconut trees and were gently shaken off; a long-haired dog stood on an open space, facing the moon by the sea and barking proudly, but after a while, he unconsciously became silent.

At this time, from the other side of the fishing village, someone was singing in a rough and loud voice:

"...We are like a group of orphans without masters, flowing from the corner of the sea to the horizon, fatigue is accompanied by hunger, hunger... However, who can pity and give us valuable bread?..."

The old man Simon Ding raised his head in a sleepwalking manner. He was moved, shrugged his shoulders slightly, and murmured to himself: "...However, who can pity and give us valuable bread?..." He shook his head silently, and then fell into painful silence again.

The night was silent, and soon the entire fishing village fell asleep in melancholy.

Night Talk

— Jiang Jiping

I like the night very much. I think the night is much more interesting than the daytime. The daytime is too noisy, and everything is too clear under the sunlight. It is not as good as under the hazy moonlight, which can evoke people's attachment. Whether it is reading or writing, it is not suitable during the day, because I often think about many things to do, and my heart is always restless. In the late night, everything cannot be done. No matter how important things are, I have to wait until tomorrow to do it, so my heart is quiet. Whether it is writing or reading; needless to say, going out for a stroll is much more interesting than during the day. If there is a moon, it will be more interesting than during the day. One day I returned from a friend's house, it was already late at night. It was still autumn, the wind was cooler, the sky was clear, and the moonlight was as white as water, making this road that I often passed look unusually beautiful. I had never seen such a scene before. I really didn't expect this road to be so annoying during the day with dust flying, people shouting, and vehicles running around. At night, it would be so quiet and beautiful that it made people so happy. Therefore, I realized that the night can enhance people's emotions; if a pair of lovers chat in the garden during the day, we don't think it's anything, but if they chat in the garden on a moonlit night, we immediately feel a kind of aesthetic feeling, as if we have read a lingering poem; the sound of the flute in the night has a deeper power to move people than during the day; if we hear the weeping of a widow during the day, we don't feel it, but it's different in the late night. Her sorrowful sound waves completely penetrate our ears, and we immediately become sad. Because the night is quiet, all the sounds are very moving: such as the sound of the night watchman's clapper, the sound of the neighbor's bell, the thin cry of selling radishes, and the barking of dogs in the distance, all seem to have the sound waves amplified by a loudspeaker, making people unable to think that this is a very ordinary sound. Immediately, there is a reaction, like finishing a sad poem or seeing a beautiful painting, that kind of feeling

I also like to read poems that describe night scenes, such as "Dog barks" Autumn in the mountains is quiet, the sound of knocking at the door tells of a monk returning at night". What: "Dream awakens to the sound of distant bells from the monastery, a pond of bright moon and lotus fragrance". All make me feel the beauty of quietness. In ancient times, there were very few prose writers who specialized in writing night scenes. I have only read two short paragraphs from Wang Wei and Qin Shaoyou. I will now record them below:

"Going north to Xuanba, the clear moon shines on the city, climbing Hua Zi Gang at night, Wang River ripples, rising and falling with the moon, cold mountain distant fire, flickering outside the forest, deep alley cold dogs, barking like leopards, village ruins night spring, echoing with sparse bells."

——Wang Wei.

"In the second year of Yuanfeng, the day after the Mid-Autumn Festival, the sky was clear, the moonlight was bright in the forest, and even the smallest hair could be counted. From Puning, passing through fifteen Buddhist temples, all were silent and no human voice was heard. By the roadside, the cottages, or the lights were hidden and revealed, the grass and trees were deep and lush, and the flowing water stopped and cried sadly, which was almost not a human realm!"

——Qin Guan.

These two pieces are written very well. I think the night is not only interesting, but also can enhance people's literary thoughts. After we are tired, we light a cigarette and think carefully about the sentences we want to write. No one will disturb us. We only hear the sound of the pen strokes on the paper. What a meaningful thing this is! Many famous writers at home and abroad have completed their masterpieces with the help of the night, right?

Writers and Language

— Zheng Boqi

Literature is the art of language, and writers should be language technicians—of course, they don't necessarily have to be language magicians. Writers and language have a destiny that cannot be separated for a moment.

Writers are not necessarily orators. In fact, many people who write well cannot speak well. However, to write well, one must have a thorough understanding and the power to use language fully. The power to drive language, although not the entire ability of a writer, is a necessary and indispensable part.

What kind of language can appropriately express a certain image of the objective, and what kind of language can appropriately express a certain emotion of the subjective, is the most important work of the writer. The great French novelist Flaubert rigorously trained Maupassant on this point.

Originally, writers are very sensitive to language. From the moment they are born, what they hear and use is the tool they use when writing. Logically, it should be easier for them to understand and use such language. But in fact, it is not the case. Language is a difficult object for writers to conquer.

If the language used by the writer is not the kind of language they have used since birth, but the language of another place or another kind of society, it is even more difficult.

There is no need to use foreign languages as an example. Just in China: it is impossible for a Cantonese person to write dialogue in Shanghai dialect, or for a rickshaw puller to write the arguments of a university professor, no matter what.

One of the major difficulties for Chinese writers now lies in this. China does not yet have a standard language, even if there is a so-called "common language," but this is not a living language that everyone has used since childhood. Therefore, when a person writes, they first feel difficulty with the tool that is most important to them. Here, we cannot help but admire Mr. Lao She. His ability to write completely in the words he speaks in daily life is something to be counted as a fortunate thing.

Many young people are imitating Mr. Lao She by writing things in Beijing dialect, but besides randomly using "nin," randomly using "zamen," randomly using "ganma," and randomly adding the "er" sound to the end of words, there is no Beijing dialect flavor at all, which instead causes readers to feel unhappy.

Lin Qinnan opposed vernacular Chinese and once said: "I fear that the vernacular Chinese of Zhejiang and Anhui is not as good as that of Zhili." This is somewhat what he said. Authors from other language families are indeed at a disadvantage in terms of language compared to authors from the Northern language family.

The revival of classical Chinese and the popularity of the recorded speech style, although there are other social backgrounds, the difficulty of language is also an important reason.

Conquering language is indeed a difficult task for modern Chinese authors.

Road Brand Products

— Li Huiying

It had been raining for three consecutive days, and Old Man Wang was stuck at home, unable to do business. Speaking of which, it was already deep winter, yet it was still raining continuously. This was something that didn't happen in the northern regions, where it usually snowed often instead. Today, the sky finally cleared up, and he was overjoyed. Facing the sun, he hurriedly brought his tools and set up his stall at his usual spot. The stall was located next to an intersection, and although the area wasn't particularly bustling, there was a decent amount of traffic. The winter morning breeze, carrying the cold, rippled along the road, stirring up the musty dampness hidden in the corners of the walls. However, the road was completely dry. If a stranger were to come, they would never believe that this was a road that had been washed by three days of rain. This was undoubtedly thanks to the good governance of the foreigners who laid the asphalt road. At this time, the sweet potato roasters, the basket-carrying sellers of large pancakes and fried dough sticks, and the congee carriers all rushed to shake off their deep sleepiness and set up shop on the road. The soy milk stall, right next to the glutinous rice seller, also set up, emitting puffs of hot air into the sky – a kind of warmth that people welcomed on winter mornings.

It was the time when people were going to and from work. Men and women walked in groups, and before long, they stopped near various food stalls to have breakfast. Rickshaw pullers, when no one was calling for them, also stopped their carts and gulped down congee. They slurped and ate quickly, as if afraid that taking too much time would cause them to lose business when someone called for a rickshaw. Old Man Wang's business also picked up. Several familiar customers, upon seeing him, first asked:

"Why haven't you been out for business these past two days?"

Then, as if remembering that it had been raining for three days and he naturally couldn't set up his stall, they quickly added:

"Oh, was it because of the rain? I forgot about that."

Some took out four copper coins, while others took out eight, to buy one or two boxes of "Road Brand" cigarettes. There were many styles of cigarette boxes. Not only did he have all kinds of Chinese brands like "Company Brand," "Golden Rat Brand," "Platinum Dragon," "Little Beauty," "Red Golden Dragon," and "Linked Pearls Brand," but he also had foreign brands like "Five Flowers Brand," "Fada'er," and "Crest." At a glance, these cigarette boxes were dazzling, but that was just because the boxes were different; the tobacco inside was all the same. People called this type of cigarette "Road Brand" because it was made on the road. Old Man Wang was currently using his small machine to produce it – this "Road Brand" product.

In the middle of the slanted surface of a small rectangular wooden box, a horizontal slit was carved out. Inside the slit, a long strip of kraft paper was rolled up, with a wooden stick rolled inside the paper. Cigarette paper coated with paste was placed flat below the horizontal slit, and tobacco was placed in the paper pocket of the horizontal slit. Then, the wooden stick was turned forward, and when it was released, the new product – a cigarette – would be revealed. Once the two ends of the cigarette were trimmed, the entire process was complete.

Old Man Wang worked diligently, and soon he had made a large pile.

"Old Man Wang, give me a pack."

Zhao Ajin, who had just finished drinking congee while sitting on the rickshaw seat, shouted loudly. Old Man Wang obediently handed over a pack, his eyes fixed on his customer, waiting for something.

Zhao Ajin, while smoking a cigarette, remembered that he hadn't paid yet, so he said:

"Old Man Wang, I'll pay you tomorrow."

The money, four copper coins, was exactly what Old Man Wang was waiting to receive. He didn't agree to "pay tomorrow." Although this was a regular customer, and logically he would definitely pay him back tomorrow, he preferred to receive cash. He didn't agree. After a moment of silence, he said with a chuckle,

"This, haha, this..."

"Alright!" the other man said, tossing four copper coins over. "Not enough to show my friendship, taking care of you all these days. Sooner or later, it's all the same! You're afraid I'll run away, aren't you? Hmph, it's only a matter of four copper coins."

After receiving the four copper coins, Old Man Wang became much more talkative:

"What are you talking about? You're a regular customer, of course, there's no problem at all. I was just joking with you. Are you angry? Then you're wrong, you're overthinking it. Money is a small matter; whether you have money or not, I can't let you go hungry."

If it's said that "old people are cunning and old horses are slippery," then it wouldn't be an exaggeration to apply that saying to Old Man Wang. He was indeed cunning, receiving the cash and also lecturing the other person. No, that's not how it should be said. Old Man Wang didn't want to give credit for a good reason; it was really difficult to do business, big or small, these days. With cash in hand, it was easier to manage. Zhao Ajin, who was naturally rough and forthright, took Old Man Wang's bad words as good words and said uneasily that he was just joking, asking Old Man Wang not to take it to heart. Old Man Wang certainly wouldn't take it to heart; making a sale was better than anything. He didn't reply any further and continued to produce "Road Brand" products.

Old Man Wang not only made "Road Brand" cigarettes, but he also smoked them himself. This was very different from the situation where ordinary workers made goods that they couldn't afford to use themselves. Now, he stopped his work and picked out a cigarette that was rolled rather badly to smoke, taking a break.

Don't underestimate this "Road Brand" small handicraft industry; even before starting work, some capital was needed. First, cigarette paper: a thousand sheets cost forty cents. Tobacco cost one dollar for four pounds. And then there were the cigarette boxes. Although ten cents could buy ten boxes, which wasn't expensive, it still added up. If you included the small machine, it would cost at least two or three dollars to get started.

Old Man Wang wasn't originally in this business. He used to work for a foreigner, sweeping the yard and tending the flower garden, what foreigners called a "coolie." He worked for one family after another for eight or nine years. Now, because he was old, he was laid off. Who would want to spend money hiring an old man with failing strength? After losing his job, he followed a friend's advice and started this business. If he didn't do this business, he couldn't afford to be idle. He was a living person and had to eat. If he was idle, he would starve to death.

He originally sold these "Road Brand" cigarettes for five copper coins a pack, but later he couldn't sell them for that price and could only sell them for four copper coins a pack, because his customers were either workers or rickshaw pullers. No one had extra money, and everyone had to count every copper coin. Another reason for his price drop was that the number of his competitors was increasing day by day. Most people were selling for four copper coins a pack, so he had to lower his price. He wasn't losing money this way. Tobacco that cost one dollar for four pounds was supposed to be sold at that price. But he knew that the tobacco in the four-copper-coin packs sold by others was actually tobacco that cost one dollar for five pounds, which should logically be sold for three and a half copper coins a pack. They were already earning more than him by selling it for four copper coins. Fortunately, smokers still had the ability to distinguish good quality from bad. After comparing and finding that the goods from other shops were inferior, they naturally preferred to buy his cigarettes, so his business hadn't declined.

The sun rose higher, and the streets became lively. The Indian policeman who managed the traffic lights came on duty. Older women and maids carried baskets to the market to buy vegetables. Cars ran in a continuous stream, and the weather gradually became warmer.

Two trash-picking children, with dirty faces, ran over from afar and stood in front of Old Man Wang, panting heavily and putting down their broken baskets. Each of them took out a large pile of empty cigarette boxes. Old Man Wang had just finished smoking his cigarette and asked the older child:

"Xiao Erzi, how many boxes did you collect?"

Then, yawning, he asked the other one:

"And you, Xiao Sanzi, how many did you bring today?"

Xiao Erzi's pile had seventeen boxes, and Xiao Sanzi's pile had fourteen boxes, for a total of thirty-one boxes. Xiao Erzi counted them again to be sure, and replied:

"A total of thirty-one, which should be – should be thirty-one copper coins."

"Thirty-one copper coins, that's right, but look at the condition of the boxes. Aren't many of them dirty?" Old Man Wang said, picking out two broken boxes to show them. "Look, can these kinds of boxes be used? Is it worth the money?"

The two children were stunned. If Old Man Wang didn't buy them, they couldn't get copper coins. How much they needed copper coins! After a while, Xiao Erzi, with a fearful heart, timidly asked Old Man Wang:

"According to you – according to you? What do you say? You – you don't want them?"

"How can I not want them?" Old Man Wang thought of a plan. "How about this, I'll take a loss and keep them all, good and bad, so it's convenient for both of us. I'll give you twenty-five copper coins. Six or seven of the boxes are unusable, so they don't count. Take these thirty copper coins," he handed them to the older child, "I'll owe you five copper coins, and we'll settle it next time. If it were anyone else, they definitely wouldn't buy such bad boxes from you. Understand?"

The two children nodded repeatedly, took the copper coins, and happily walked away, discussing where to spend them and how to spend them.

Old Man Wang understood the tricks of doing business; if you want to make money, you have to be clever everywhere. Now he used those empty boxes that he had said were unusable first, laughing at his cleverness in exploiting labor.

"Old Man Wang, is your business good these days?"

Suddenly hearing this deep voice, Old Man Wang was stunned for a moment, then guessed who it was. He wasn't wrong; it was the kind man who had first brought him here to do business and occupy this spot. Without his help, he wouldn't have been able to do this business. He knew the importance of gratitude and should show his appreciation. Old Man Wang hurriedly stood up and handed over a pack of cigarettes. This was his small way of expressing his gratitude, and he didn't begrudge this small expense. He said with a smile:

"Sir, thanks to you, business is still good. Have a pack and try it. Why are you so free today, sir? I haven't seen you lately. You must be too busy, right?"

The Sixth Master smoked "Platinum Dragon" and didn't want his "Road Brand." This left Old Man Wang at a loss. How could he be at peace when he couldn't repay his benefactor? He was very careful when talking to his benefactor. If he accidentally said something wrong and offended the Sixth Master, his business would be difficult to continue. Therefore, Old Man Wang spoke every word with great caution, which was very different from his attitude when talking to Zhao Ajin and Xiao Erzi.

The Sixth Master had already walked past. Although Old Man Wang hadn't given away the cigarettes, he knew that he hadn't offended his benefactor. As for why his benefactor didn't greet him more, it was because his time was valuable and he was a person of status, so logically he wouldn't chat with him much.

He sat down and started working again, rolling cigarettes one by one.

Someone nearby was calling him:

"Old Man Wang, another pack of cigarettes."

Old Man Wang stopped working, delivered a pack of cigarettes to the customer, and collected the money. Just as he returned to his spot, he heard someone calling him again:

"Old Man Wang, another pack of cigarettes."

Old Man Wang's business was really good today. He was very happy, and his stomach was rumbling. Looking at the sweet potato stall behind him, where the sweet potatoes were roasting, he couldn't help but shout:

"Hey! One sweet potato, please."

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Informal Discussion

Reading "Population Problem and Birth Control"

— Shi Ji

Following Mrs. Sanger, Mrs. Martin has also arrived in Shanghai and gave a public lecture yesterday entitled: "Population Problems and Birth Control."

According to the lecture reported in the newspapers, the significance of this lecture can be summarized in the following sentences: "No matter what country, if it cannot provide its people with a comfortable life, it should advocate birth control. The advocacy of childbearing should be determined by the ability of the producers."

Mrs. Martin saw that "before social systems are reformed, there are millions of children groaning in the painful hunger and cold life." She saw that among the "two million unemployed people in England," "their children rarely have the opportunity to receive education," so she advocated "reproduction should only occur after parents have work."

"After the parents have work," will their children then have the "opportunity to receive education"? This is doubtful. In our country's situation, the only children of the proletariat who lack even food and clothing are truly everywhere. Taking a step back, "after their parents have work," the children are born, but what if the parents become unemployed again? Again, considering our country's situation, due to various external and internal reasons, the decline of middle- and upper-class families has been very prevalent in recent years. Based on this, shouldn't we only "control births," but simply eliminate births altogether.

Furthermore, saying "We should only produce as many children as our economic situation allows us to raise and nurture" seems to imply that only the children of the wealthy can become good members of society. Is this the case in reality? Not to mention distant examples, even the newspapers of the day have the example of a "scandalous bankruptcy" case of the son of a wealthy businessman. This shows that the sons of the wealthy are not necessarily "good" members.

People are determined by their living environment. "Having a garden without children" and "having children without a garden" are the best explanations for this social system. Because there are "millions of children" "groaning in the painful hunger and cold life," we shouldn't have "millions of children." That is such a ridiculous method of carving a mark on a boat while searching for a lost sword!

Finally, Mrs. Martin also compared the infant mortality rates of England and India, saying that "both places have civic education. Now the living standards in England have improved, and life is happy, while India is the opposite. The difference is that the British can control births, while the Indians cannot." It seems that India's being "the opposite" is entirely due to a lack of birth control.

Is the poverty of colonial India really caused by a lack of birth control? In all aspects of treatment, is it the same as England, which is "ruled by the same government"? I think that anyone who pays even a little attention to the recent situation in the world can easily answer this. We should expose this kind of whitewashing that serves as a mouthpiece for imperialism.

Even in England, where "living standards have improved and life is happy," aren't there also "two million" unemployed people and their children who have "rarely an opportunity to receive education"? What exactly does "happy life" refer to? They are enjoying the same fate as the slaves in the colonies.

The motivation of reformism or humanitarianism may be beyond reproach, but in terms of objective effect, it often becomes a tool for anesthetizing the masses, causing the masses to hesitate and wait, and as a result, the masses still become meat on the chopping block.

Advocates of birth control are just like other reformists. What they do is only to ask society to make concessions, not to fight against society, so the only effect is to make the masses wait with bated breath to be stabbed! Moreover, under the smoke screen of birth control, there is also a hidden meaning of preaching for imperialists.

Little Woman

— Ye Ge

This little woman is the wife of You San, a private in the 3rd artillery battalion. She is a slender, calm, gentle, and sincere young woman. A stranger, a visiting merchant, would never believe that she is already a married woman, and even a woman who already has a six-year-old daughter.

When You San, unable to make a living in the village, carried his bundle and went to join the army, he told her, "Take good care of the child. I think that as long as I can make some money, I'll be back in a year or two!" He smiled gently, but it was such a miserable, sad smile. He strode away under the locust tree and disappeared, never to be seen again. However, that was already three years ago.

You San had already joined the army, and the family lacked manpower. At the same time, they couldn't afford to hire anyone. She had to mortgage the one and a half acres of thin land at home to a relative in a neighboring village, borrow some money, and set up a few tables and benches in the spacious thatched house at home, opening a small tavern and a "twelve-branch game" (Note: a type of gambling tool) establishment.

The business immediately flourished. The farmers frantically emerged from every broken thatched house and every small corner in the village, and quickly crowded into her thatched house, shouting loudly. Because of drunkenness, wine glasses were poured into nostrils. Fathers and children fought over three and a half sentences that they didn't understand. Gamblers, over two or three small silver coins, fought with their fists beating their chests. Until our landlady ran down from her dirty counter and said gently:

"Everyone, how terrible this is, how terrible! It's just like a market..."

Then the commotion subsided. People returned to their proper seats, rational discussions and debates again filled the narrow venue.

This little woman sometimes got drunk herself, because crowds of young farmers called out to her so intimately:

"Sister-in-law You San, let's have a drink to bless Brother You San with success!..."

So they raised their glasses high and poured them straight down their throats, and she began to feel uneasy and anxious. She was accustomed to feeling a kind of urgency whenever someone used an intimate tone to call her husband's name. This feeling often drove her half-crazy. At this time, her eyes burned with unease, and her mind was constantly burning with him, a strong young farmer with broad shoulders and chest, and a simple smile that bordered on stupidity. So she smiled too, and unconsciously picked up the wine dipper and drew homemade white liquor from the jar, pouring bowl after bowl into her parched throat, until her pale face flushed red, and her eyes burned with fiery flames. Her senses began to blur, and she felt that the air in the house was so suffocating and turbid that it almost made her want to vomit. Really, at this time she longed for air, for relief and comfort, even if it was just a little. So she locked her money box, told her six-year-old daughter to sit and watch the store, strode out the door and ran. The gamblers were busy with their twelve-branch game. The drunks were snoring on the table. But several young half-asleep fellows followed her out. At

Nora (21)

— Written by Wan Chao-chen, Explained by Xin Xin

Nora was sadly thinking of going out to drown herself when Helmer forcefully pushed open the door!

Helmer: Nora! You damned woman! Look at the good deed you've done!

Nora: (staring at her husband, coldly answering) I now fully understand.

Helmer: You have ruined my lifelong happiness, you have ruined my future. I am now sent into the hands of that scoundrel to be extorted by him. I have no choice but to comply with everything he says! As for the two of us, we will still act as husband and wife on the outside. As for the children, I dare not entrust them to you. From now on, there will be no more talk of happiness or unhappiness, only covering up and putting on a facade. Just as Helmer was furious, the maid Eileen delivered another letter. Helmer read a few lines and jumped up, saying: Nora, we are saved, we are both fine! (After throwing the IOU and the outer envelope into the stove to burn.) Nora, I know you did all that for love of me, please don't take it to heart. I swear, I have already forgiven you.

Nora: Thank you for forgiving me! (Exits to the right)

the door, there was an open field. She ran at a large stride, like crazy, and the young farmers chased behind her, lightly whistling and softly calling.

They chased, in the fields, in the meadows, and finally disappeared into the groves on the hillside. She stopped and hesitated. In her blurred mind, she imagined a shadow, a familiar shadow that she had loved and hugged. At this time, it was covered in blood and collapsed there, not far from her in the field. But when she looked closely, it was gone. She thought, "Surely, he won't be back. He's dead!" So, heartbroken, she cried in a muffled voice.

It wasn't until her slender arms were grabbed by several strong hands, and her body was also suspended, that she realized that there were still people following behind her. Who were following? Young, strong, as lovely and brave as You San. However, she felt a sense of insulted anger. Because she felt that she had been dragged by these thugs into the depths of the hillside grove, into that secluded grove where young men and women meet, and was gently pressed down, someone was tearing open her clothes, someone was groping her chest, someone was... She was furious. She sobered up from the wine. She suddenly realized that she was being insulted and harmed by unreasonable violence. However, she couldn't struggle. People held her down tightly, so she suddenly screamed, shouting in an angry tone:

"You dogs, you bully me so well! You San told me he's coming back tomorrow morning!..."

You San, You San, a rough private in the artillery! The young farmers trembled. They had all suffered under him, and no one in the village was afraid of him, but they had now insulted his wife, a gentle, lovely little woman. So everyone gently let go, jumped, and rolled out like a rubber ball.

When she returned home from the fields, it was already late at night. The twelve-branch game had broken up, the drunks had dispersed, and her six-year-old daughter was still sitting on the counter, dozing off like a clever little shopkeeper. She ran to her, gently stroked her hair, and cried in a muffled voice.

Ode to Freedom

Farmers, merchants, workers, students, and soldiers, everyone with one heart, regardless of gender, working together for the future. We must not forget the mission of national salvation. We are the masters of China! Masters of China! Masters of China! Don't cling to your broken homes! Don't cherish your empty dreams! Press down on your wounds! Stand up straight! Fight back for the freedom and liberation of our nation! Freedom and liberation! Freedom and liberation! Put on the same armor! Step into the battlefield of life! Raise your defensive swords and guns! Stop the enemy's rampant behavior! Fight back for the freedom and liberation of our nation! China has broken through its dark night; the people have tempered their will into steel. The future has shown the hope of light. Look! Look at the flames of self-salvation that burn all around!

Cai Xiaofang's Mao Family Letter China and West (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening: "The Shepherd's Scroll"

Crushing the enemy and achieving success, returning home in glory. Zhu Chundeng received the imperial decree to return to his hometown. But who knew? He didn't see his kind mother or his wife. He hurriedly called for his aunt to ask what had happened. The wolf-hearted woman had a silver tongue. She said that the mother and daughter-in-law had gone to the afterlife. Hearing this was like a thunderbolt. His heart was broken with hatred. He held a memorial service and helped the poor. He performed good deeds to pray for the departed souls. But who knew? The mother and daughter-in-law were still alive. They had suffered family disasters and were hiding in the deep mountains. The shepherd lived with his flock. He looked at his family but dared not return. He swallowed his tears and endured the hardship of begging. Husband and wife met at the tomb. Looking at their faces, they were surprised and suspicious. After a thorough questioning, the truth came to light. Only then did he know that his aunt's conscience was wounded. His mother cried until her tears were dry. On the spot, he changed into official robes and received imperial decrees. After suffering came sweetness, and his eyebrows finally relaxed. The wicked woman was anxious at this time. She knelt in the center and swore to dispel suspicions. But who knew? Before the oath was finished, a blue dragon arrived. In an instant, she turned to ashes. One cannot escape the consequences of their own evil deeds.

Afterglow

The "Husheng Bi-Monthly" magazine issued by Husheng Publishing House at 744 Niuzhuang Road, in addition to literature, film, broadcasting, entertainment, drama, essays, etc., also has "Dance Art" news edited by He Huashen and Leng Bing, with very rich content. The table of contents includes essays such as "Zhu Huizhen's Nude Photo," "Chen Jingfang After Going to Sea," "Ascending the Volcano," "From Dance Hostesses to Dance Hostess Supply Stations," "Towing Diary," etc., numbering more than a dozen articles. It is scheduled to be published on the 20th. All circles are welcome to give guidance and criticism. For detailed table of contents, please see the advertisements in various newspapers on the 19th. All newsstands and major bookstores are selling it.

From 10:00 PM to 11:00 PM every afternoon, Xin Xin Radio broadcasts Xing Junming's Mandarin storytelling "Falling Rosy Clouds and Lonely Wild Ducks."

The Children's Broadcasting Troupe, organized by several elementary school children in this city, is led by the school's teachers to broadcast and sing children's songs, instilling children's voices with educational significance, with a pure purpose. It is now heard that the troupe will broadcast programs on Zhongxi Radio every Sunday morning from 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM starting this week. All circles are welcome to give instructions. The troupe's address is transferred to Jingming Elementary School, 77 Fuyou Road, Nanshi.

In addition to various special issues attached to each issue of Dasheng Daily, a Microphone Weekly has now been added every Sunday, specializing in photos and news from the broadcasting industry, which is said to be edited by Yingyin Amateur Society. All circles are welcome to submit contributions and subscribe.

Movie News

Little Miss Marker Premieres in Paris

"Little Miss Marker" is Shirley Temple's most successful masterpiece, with songs and dances, and full of fun, which can be called the highest peak of the eighth art. Shirley dances the hula, plays an old woman, and performs a one-act play in the film, every move is endearing. The Paris authorities are serious about selecting films. In order to cater to the audience's psychology, taking advantage of this spring holiday, they will premiere it today after "A Farewell to Arms."

Laurel and Hardy's New Work "Block-Heads"

Nanjing Screening

Silver Jottings

— Zhi Er

Since Chen Ningqiu joined the Shanghai Theater, the checks from the theatrical seniors have been issued again, and there are as many as four (two are still pending). Although the previously issued "Red Light in the Darkness" was given as the second installment. Now let's just write a short note for now: First time, "Poverty is Not a Crime", scheduled to be staged around the end of April or early May; Second time, "Red Light in the Darkness", "Thirty Million Refugees"; Third time, "Thunderstorm"; Fourth time, "William Tell".

Also, some people are saying that I am obviously a "bourgeois" figure. Many people seem to see me more clearly than I see myself.

The propaganda for "Go to Nature" has been written very lively recently, but it is said that the official release date is still in mid-June.

Li Lili asked someone to send out a message for her: her performance for the Bright Moon Society is completely voluntary. Therefore, this miscellaneous note is written as above, to serve as a message.

Zhang Zhiyun, Xu Qinfang and others went to Southeast Asia with the Star Troupe to sell their talents for money. The stars who stayed in Shanghai, in addition to unveiling satin shops and "crowning" the queen of dance, also helped out on stage. Recently, following Li Minghui, Yang Naimei also joined "The Comedian" for a while.

Yang Naimei seems to have said that if she had the opportunity, she was planning to make another film as a memorial. Could it be that bringing out the title of a former movie star and making an appearance on stage like this would serve as a memorial?
